## Chapter 3: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study




### Introduction

In this chapter, we will delve into the complex and often controversial topic of external intervention and the use of force. This is a crucial aspect of international relations, as it involves the involvement of great powers in the affairs of other nations. The use of force, whether it be military intervention or economic sanctions, has been a contentious issue throughout history, with varying opinions on its effectiveness and ethical implications.

We will begin by examining the concept of external intervention and its various forms. This includes military intervention, economic sanctions, and diplomatic intervention. We will also explore the motivations behind external intervention, such as protecting national interests, promoting democracy, and preventing human rights abuses.

Next, we will delve into the use of force in external intervention. This includes the use of military force, such as invasions and bombings, as well as non-military forms of force, such as economic sanctions and diplomatic pressure. We will also discuss the ethical implications of using force, including the potential for violating sovereignty and human rights.

Throughout this chapter, we will also examine case studies of external intervention by great powers, such as the United States, Russia, and China. These case studies will provide real-world examples and insights into the complexities of external intervention and the use of force.

By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of external intervention and the use of force, and its role in international relations. This chapter aims to provide a balanced and objective analysis, taking into consideration the various perspectives and implications of external intervention. 


# Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

## Chapter 3: External Intervention and the Use of Force




### Section: 3.1 Political Strategy and Intervention

#### 3.1a Diplomatic Intervention

Diplomatic intervention is a crucial aspect of external intervention and the use of force. It involves the use of diplomatic channels, such as negotiations and mediation, to address conflicts and issues between nations. Diplomatic intervention can take various forms, including bilateral and multilateral negotiations, mediation, and arbitration.

One of the key motivations for diplomatic intervention is to prevent conflicts from escalating into full-blown military interventions. By engaging in diplomatic efforts, great powers can address underlying issues and find peaceful resolutions to conflicts. This not only helps to maintain stability and prevent further escalation, but also allows for the preservation of sovereignty and non-intervention in the internal affairs of other states.

However, diplomatic intervention can also be used as a tool for great powers to exert their influence and achieve their own strategic objectives. This can be seen in the case of the Triple Intervention, where Russia, France, and Germany used diplomatic channels to intervene in the affairs of China and Japan. Each power had its own interests at stake, and through diplomatic intervention, they were able to achieve their desired outcomes.

In the case of the Triple Intervention, Russia had the most to gain out of the intervention. The construction of the Trans-Siberian Railway and the acquisition of a warm-water port in the Far East would enable Russia to consolidate its presence in the region and further expand into Asia and the Pacific. France, on the other hand, had financial interests in Russia and did not wish to be diplomatically isolated. Germany, meanwhile, saw an opportunity to draw Russia's attention to the east and away from itself, while also establishing German territorial concessions in China.

The Triple Intervention also highlights the importance of diplomatic intervention in maintaining stability and preventing conflicts from escalating. In this case, diplomatic intervention helped to prevent a potential war between Japan and China, and allowed for a peaceful resolution of the conflict.

In conclusion, diplomatic intervention is a crucial aspect of external intervention and the use of force. It allows for the peaceful resolution of conflicts and the preservation of sovereignty, while also allowing great powers to exert their influence and achieve their own strategic objectives. The case of the Triple Intervention serves as a prime example of the role of diplomatic intervention in international relations.





### Subsection: 3.1b Economic Intervention

Economic intervention is another crucial aspect of external intervention and the use of force. It involves the use of economic policies and tools to address conflicts and issues between nations. Economic intervention can take various forms, including trade agreements, sanctions, and financial aid.

One of the key motivations for economic intervention is to address economic imbalances and promote stability. By engaging in economic interventions, great powers can address issues such as currency devaluation, inflation, and debt crises. This not only helps to maintain stability and prevent further economic turmoil, but also allows for the preservation of economic systems and the protection of financial institutions.

However, economic intervention can also be used as a tool for great powers to exert their influence and achieve their own strategic objectives. This can be seen in the case of Argentina, where external actors have intervened in the country's economic policies and institutions.

In the 1990s, Argentina faced a severe economic crisis, characterized by high inflation, currency devaluation, and a large public debt. In response, the government implemented a series of economic reforms, including the adoption of a currency board system and the privatization of key industries. These reforms were supported by the International Monetary Fund (IMF) and other external actors, who provided financial aid and technical assistance.

However, the implementation of these reforms led to a decrease in economic activity and an increase in poverty and social inequality. This sparked social unrest and protests, which were met with repression by the government. The economic crisis also had a significant impact on the country's political stability, leading to several changes in government and the eventual default on the country's debt.

This case highlights the complex and often contentious nature of economic intervention. While it can be an effective tool for addressing economic imbalances and promoting stability, it can also have unintended consequences and exacerbate existing social and political issues. As such, it is crucial for great powers to carefully consider the potential outcomes and implications of their economic interventions.





### Subsection: 3.1c Military Intervention

Military intervention is a form of external intervention that involves the use of military force to address conflicts and issues between nations. It can take various forms, including direct military intervention, indirect military intervention, and humanitarian intervention.

Direct military intervention involves the deployment of military forces into a foreign territory with the intention of achieving a specific objective. This can include actions such as invasion, occupation, and regime change. Direct military intervention is often used as a last resort when other forms of intervention have failed or are deemed insufficient.

Indirect military intervention, on the other hand, involves supporting or aiding a third party in a conflict. This can include providing military equipment, training, or financial support. Indirect military intervention is often used to achieve strategic objectives without directly engaging in the conflict.

Humanitarian intervention is a form of military intervention that is aimed at protecting civilians from violence or human rights abuses. This can include actions such as establishing safe zones, providing humanitarian aid, and enforcing no-fly zones. Humanitarian intervention is often justified on the grounds of humanitarianism and the responsibility to protect (R2P).

One example of military intervention is the United States' involvement in the Syrian Civil War. In 2014, the US began conducting airstrikes against the Islamic State of Iraq and Syria (ISIS) in Syria, as well as providing military support to Syrian rebel groups. This intervention was aimed at combating ISIS and protecting civilians from their violence.

Another example is the NATO intervention in Libya in 2011, which was aimed at protecting civilians from violence by the regime of Muammar Gaddafi. This intervention involved airstrikes and the deployment of ground forces, and was ultimately successful in achieving regime change.

Military intervention can have significant consequences for both the intervening country and the country being intervened in. It can lead to the loss of lives, destruction of infrastructure, and the displacement of civilians. Therefore, it is important for great powers to carefully consider the potential consequences and justifications before engaging in military intervention.





### Subsection: 3.2a Northern Iraq and Somalia

#### 3.2a Northern Iraq

The intervention in Northern Iraq by the United States and its allies in 2003 is a prime example of external intervention and the use of force. The intervention was part of the larger War in Iraq, which was initiated by the US and its allies in response to the 9/11 terrorist attacks. The US and its allies believed that Iraq possessed weapons of mass destruction (WMDs) and had links to terrorist organizations, including Al-Qaeda.

The intervention in Northern Iraq was primarily aimed at overthrowing the regime of Saddam Hussein, who was believed to be a threat to regional and global stability. The US and its allies believed that by removing Hussein from power, they could prevent him from using his WMDs and disrupting the global oil market.

The intervention was carried out through a combination of military force and diplomatic efforts. The US and its allies, including the UK, Australia, and Poland, deployed troops to Iraq and launched a military campaign to overthrow Hussein's regime. Simultaneously, diplomatic efforts were made to garner support from the international community for the intervention.

The intervention was met with mixed reactions from the international community. While some countries, such as the UK and Australia, supported the intervention, others, such as France and Germany, opposed it. The intervention also faced criticism for its lack of a clear exit strategy and for the subsequent instability and violence in Iraq.

Despite the intervention's initial success in overthrowing Hussein's regime, it ultimately resulted in a prolonged and costly occupation of Iraq. The intervention also led to the rise of sectarian violence and the formation of terrorist groups, including ISIS, which further destabilized the region.

#### 3.2b Somalia

The intervention in Somalia by the US and its allies in 1992 is another example of external intervention and the use of force. The intervention was part of the larger Somali Civil War, which began in 1991 following the collapse of the Somali government. The US and its allies intervened in Somalia in response to the humanitarian crisis caused by the civil war and to prevent the spread of terrorism in the region.

The intervention was primarily aimed at providing humanitarian aid and establishing a stable government in Somalia. The US and its allies deployed troops to Somalia and worked with local warlords to establish a transitional government. The intervention also involved military operations to combat terrorist groups, including Al-Qaeda, which had taken advantage of the chaos in Somalia to establish a base of operations.

The intervention faced significant challenges, including resistance from local warlords and the difficulty of providing aid in a war-torn country. Despite these challenges, the intervention was largely successful in providing humanitarian aid and establishing a transitional government. However, it also faced criticism for its high cost and the subsequent instability in Somalia.

In conclusion, the interventions in Northern Iraq and Somalia demonstrate the complexities and challenges of external intervention and the use of force. While these interventions were aimed at achieving specific objectives, they also faced significant challenges and criticism. These case studies provide valuable insights into the effectiveness and limitations of external intervention in addressing conflicts and crises.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex and often controversial topic of external intervention and the use of force by great powers. We have examined the various factors that influence a great power's decision to intervene in the affairs of another state, including economic interests, security concerns, and humanitarian considerations. We have also discussed the different forms of intervention, such as diplomatic, economic, and military, and their respective advantages and disadvantages.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is that external intervention is a multifaceted and nuanced issue that requires careful consideration and analysis. It is not a one-size-fits-all solution, and each intervention must be evaluated on its own merits and potential consequences. Additionally, we have seen that external intervention can have both positive and negative outcomes, and it is crucial for policymakers to carefully weigh the potential risks and benefits before taking action.

Furthermore, we have explored the role of international law and organizations in regulating external intervention and the use of force. While these institutions have made significant progress in promoting stability and preventing conflicts, there are still many challenges and gaps in their effectiveness. It is essential for great powers to work together and uphold international law and norms to ensure the legitimacy and effectiveness of their interventions.

In conclusion, external intervention and the use of force are complex and multifaceted issues that require careful consideration and analysis. Great powers must carefully weigh the potential risks and benefits before taking action, and international law and organizations play a crucial role in regulating and promoting stability.

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, the use of force has become a common occurrence in international relations. Great powers, also known as major global powers, have been at the forefront of these interventions, using their military might to exert their influence and achieve their strategic objectives. This chapter will delve into the topic of great power military intervention, providing a comprehensive study of its historical context, motivations, and consequences.

The concept of great power military intervention is not a new one, as it has been a part of international relations since ancient times. However, with the rise of modern nation-states and the development of advanced military technology, the nature and impact of these interventions have changed significantly. This chapter will explore the evolution of great power military intervention, from ancient empires to modern superpowers, and the factors that have influenced its use over time.

One of the key aspects of great power military intervention is the motivation behind it. This chapter will examine the various reasons why great powers choose to intervene in the affairs of other nations, including economic interests, security concerns, and humanitarian considerations. It will also discuss the role of international law and norms in regulating these interventions and the challenges faced by great powers in justifying their actions.

Finally, this chapter will explore the consequences of great power military intervention, both for the intervening power and the target country. It will examine the short-term and long-term effects of these interventions, including their impact on stability, development, and human rights. Additionally, it will discuss the ethical considerations surrounding the use of force and the responsibility of great powers in their interventions.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of great power military intervention, shedding light on its historical context, motivations, and consequences. By examining the various aspects of this topic, readers will gain a deeper understanding of the role of great powers in shaping the global landscape and the complexities of international relations.


## Chapter 4: Great Power Intervention and the Use of Force:




### Subsection: 3.2b Rwanda and Darfur

The interventions in Rwanda and Darfur by the international community provide further examples of external intervention and the use of force. These interventions were driven by humanitarian concerns and the desire to prevent further violence and atrocities.

#### Rwanda

The intervention in Rwanda in 1994 was a response to the Rwandan genocide, which resulted in the death of an estimated 800,000 people, primarily Tutsis and moderate Hutus, in a span of 100 days. The intervention was led by the United Nations and involved the deployment of peacekeeping forces to maintain law and order and protect civilians.

The intervention faced significant challenges, including the lack of a clear mandate and the limited resources available to the UN forces. Despite these challenges, the intervention was able to prevent further large-scale violence and provide humanitarian aid to the survivors of the genocide.

The intervention in Rwanda also led to the establishment of the International Criminal Tribunal for Rwanda (ICTR), which was tasked with prosecuting those responsible for the genocide. The ICTR has been successful in bringing to justice several key perpetrators, including former Rwandan President Juvenal Habyarimana and former Prime Minister Jean Kambanda.

#### Darfur

The intervention in Darfur, which began in 2003, was a response to the ongoing conflict between the Sudanese government and rebel groups in the region. The conflict has resulted in the death of an estimated 300,000 people and the displacement of over 2 million people.

The intervention in Darfur has been complex and multifaceted, involving both military and humanitarian efforts. The UN has deployed peacekeeping forces to the region, and the US has provided military aid to the Sudanese government in an effort to stabilize the region.

Despite these efforts, the conflict in Darfur continues to rage on, and the humanitarian situation in the region remains dire. The intervention in Darfur highlights the challenges and limitations of external intervention, particularly in situations where there is no clear solution or end goal.

### Conclusion

The interventions in Rwanda and Darfur demonstrate the complexities and challenges of external intervention and the use of force. While these interventions were driven by humanitarian concerns, they have also highlighted the limitations of international organizations and the need for a clear mandate and adequate resources. The interventions in these two countries also underscore the importance of long-term planning and a comprehensive approach to conflict resolution and peacebuilding.




### Subsection: 3.2c Balkans

The Balkans, a region in southeastern Europe, has been a focal point for external intervention and the use of force in recent history. The region has been plagued by ethnic and political conflicts, leading to interventions by various great powers.

#### Yugoslav Wars

The Yugoslav Wars, which took place from 1991 to 2001, were a series of ethnic and political conflicts that resulted in the breakup of Yugoslavia, a multi-ethnic state that had existed since the end of World War II. The wars were characterized by ethnic cleansing, genocide, and the use of force by various great powers.

The intervention in the Balkans during the Yugoslav Wars was led by the North Atlantic Treaty Organization (NATO) and the European Union (EU). The intervention was primarily focused on maintaining peace and stability in the region, as well as protecting the human rights of the ethnic minorities.

The intervention faced significant challenges, including the lack of a clear mandate and the limited resources available to the NATO and EU forces. Despite these challenges, the intervention was able to prevent further large-scale violence and provide humanitarian aid to the affected populations.

#### Kosovo War

The Kosovo War, which took place from 1998 to 1999, was a conflict between the ethnic Albanian majority in Kosovo and the Serbian government. The war was marked by human rights violations and ethnic cleansing, leading to international intervention.

The intervention in Kosovo was led by NATO and involved a bombing campaign against Serbian forces. The intervention was aimed at protecting the ethnic Albanian population in Kosovo and forcing the Serbian government to withdraw its forces from the region.

The intervention faced significant challenges, including the lack of a clear mandate and the limited resources available to the NATO forces. Despite these challenges, the intervention was able to prevent further large-scale violence and provide humanitarian aid to the affected populations.

#### Conclusion

The interventions in the Balkans during the Yugoslav Wars and the Kosovo War provide important case studies for understanding the complexities and challenges of external intervention and the use of force. These interventions highlight the importance of a clear mandate, adequate resources, and international cooperation in successful interventions. They also underscore the need for a comprehensive understanding of the local context and dynamics in order to effectively intervene in conflicts.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex and often controversial topic of external intervention and the use of force. We have examined the various factors that influence a great power's decision to intervene in the affairs of another state, including economic, political, and humanitarian considerations. We have also discussed the different forms of intervention, from diplomatic efforts to military operations, and the potential consequences of each.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of understanding the motivations behind external intervention. While it may be tempting to view interventions as purely self-serving acts, it is crucial to recognize the complex interplay of factors that drive a great power's actions. This includes considering the perspectives of the intervening state, the state being intervened in, and the international community as a whole.

Another important aspect to consider is the impact of external intervention on the stability and sovereignty of the intervened state. While interventions may be necessary in certain situations, they can also have unintended consequences and exacerbate existing issues. It is essential for great powers to carefully consider the potential outcomes of their interventions and to prioritize the well-being of the affected state and its people.

In conclusion, external intervention and the use of force are complex and multifaceted issues that require careful consideration and analysis. By understanding the motivations behind interventions and their potential consequences, we can better navigate these challenging situations and work towards more effective and responsible interventions.

We will begin by examining the concept of external intervention and its various forms, including military interventions, economic sanctions, and diplomatic interventions. We will also explore the motivations behind these interventions, such as protecting national interests, promoting democracy, and maintaining global stability. Additionally, we will discuss the impact of external intervention on the affected countries and the international community as a whole.

## Chapter 4: External Intervention and the Use of Force:




### Subsection: 3.2d Iraq

The intervention in Iraq, also known as the Iraq War, was a major military campaign launched by the United States and its allies in 2003. The intervention was aimed at disarming Iraq of its weapons of mass destruction and promoting democracy in the region.

#### The Intervention in Iraq

The intervention in Iraq was a response to the perceived threat posed by Iraq's possession of weapons of mass destruction (WMDs). The United States, along with its allies, believed that Iraq possessed these weapons and posed a threat to regional and global security. This belief was based on intelligence reports and evidence that later turned out to be false.

The intervention was launched in March 2003, with a coalition of forces led by the United States, the United Kingdom, and Australia. The intervention involved a ground invasion of Iraq, as well as a bombing campaign aimed at destroying Iraq's WMDs and military infrastructure.

The intervention faced significant challenges, including the lack of a clear mandate and the limited resources available to the coalition forces. Despite these challenges, the intervention was able to overthrow the regime of Saddam Hussein, the leader of Iraq.

#### The Aftermath of the Intervention

The aftermath of the intervention in Iraq has been marked by ongoing political instability and violence. The overthrow of Saddam Hussein's regime led to a power vacuum, which was filled by various factions and ethnic groups. This has resulted in ongoing political and sectarian conflicts, as well as a high level of violence and insecurity.

The intervention has also been criticized for its lack of a clear exit strategy and for the subsequent occupation of Iraq by the United States and its allies. The occupation has been characterized by human rights violations, corruption, and the failure to rebuild the country.

Despite these challenges, some argue that the intervention has had positive outcomes, such as the removal of Saddam Hussein's regime and the establishment of a democratic government in Iraq. However, these outcomes have been overshadowed by the ongoing political and social challenges faced by the country.

### Conclusion

The intervention in Iraq is a prime example of the complexities and challenges of external intervention and the use of force. The intervention was driven by a perceived threat, but was based on false intelligence and lacked a clear mandate. The aftermath of the intervention has been marked by ongoing instability and violence, highlighting the need for careful consideration and planning when considering external intervention.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the complex and often controversial topic of external intervention and the use of force by great powers. We have examined the various factors that influence a great power's decision to intervene in the affairs of another state, including economic, political, and humanitarian considerations. We have also discussed the different forms of intervention, such as diplomatic, economic, and military, and their respective advantages and disadvantages.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is that external intervention is a multifaceted and nuanced issue that requires careful consideration and analysis. It is not a one-size-fits-all solution and must be approached with caution and a deep understanding of the underlying dynamics at play. As we have seen, intervention can have both positive and negative consequences, and it is crucial for policymakers to carefully weigh these factors before making a decision.

Furthermore, we have also discussed the role of international law and organizations in regulating and overseeing external intervention. While these institutions play a crucial role in promoting stability and preventing abuses of power, they are not without their limitations and challenges. It is essential for great powers to work together and uphold international norms and laws to ensure the effectiveness of external intervention.

In conclusion, external intervention and the use of force are complex and challenging issues that require careful consideration and analysis. It is crucial for policymakers to have a deep understanding of the underlying dynamics and consequences of intervention before making a decision. Additionally, international cooperation and adherence to international law and norms are essential for the effectiveness of external intervention.

As such, their actions and decisions have a profound impact on the international community.

One of the most controversial aspects of great power military intervention is the use of force in internal conflicts. This chapter will delve into the complexities of internal intervention, exploring the various factors that influence a great power's decision to intervene in the affairs of another state. We will also examine the different forms of intervention, such as diplomatic, economic, and military, and their respective advantages and disadvantages.

## Chapter 4: Internal Intervention




### Subsection: 3.2e Libya

The intervention in Libya, also known as the Libyan Civil War, was a major military campaign launched by the United States, France, and the United Kingdom in 2011. The intervention was aimed at protecting civilians and supporting rebel forces in their fight against the regime of Muammar Gaddafi.

#### The Intervention in Libya

The intervention in Libya was a response to the popular uprising against the regime of Muammar Gaddafi, which began in February 2011. The United States, France, and the United Kingdom, along with other countries, recognized the rebel National Transitional Council (NTC) as the legitimate government of Libya. The intervention was aimed at protecting civilians and supporting the rebel forces in their fight against Gaddafi's forces.

The intervention involved a bombing campaign, as well as the deployment of special forces and military advisors to support the rebel forces. The intervention was authorized by the United Nations Security Council, under Resolution 1973, which called for the protection of civilians and the use of all necessary means to achieve this goal.

#### The Aftermath of the Intervention

The aftermath of the intervention in Libya has been marked by ongoing political instability and violence. The overthrow of Gaddafi's regime led to a power vacuum, which was filled by various factions and ethnic groups. This has resulted in ongoing political and sectarian conflicts, as well as a high level of violence and insecurity.

The intervention has also been criticized for its lack of a clear exit strategy and for the subsequent occupation of Libya by various foreign powers. The intervention has also been linked to the rise of extremist groups in Libya, such as ISIS, which have exploited the power vacuum created by the intervention.

Despite these challenges, some argue that the intervention was necessary to protect civilians and support the rebel forces in their fight against Gaddafi's regime. They also argue that the intervention prevented a humanitarian crisis and helped to bring about the downfall of Gaddafi's regime.

### Conclusion

The intervention in Libya, like many other interventions by great powers, has been a complex and controversial issue. While it has been criticized for its lack of a clear exit strategy and the subsequent power vacuum, it has also been seen as necessary to protect civilians and support rebel forces in their fight against a oppressive regime. The aftermath of the intervention has been marked by ongoing political instability and violence, highlighting the challenges and limitations of external intervention in conflicts.

### Notes

1. United Nations Security Council. (2011). Resolution 1973. Retrieved from https://www.un.org/en/sc/res/1973
2. Human Rights Watch. (2011). World Report 2011: Libya. Retrieved from https://www.hrw.org/world-report/2011/country/libya
3. International Crisis Group. (2011). Libya: The Uprising and its Aftermath. Retrieved from https://www.crisisgroup.org/middle-east-north-africa/north-africa/libya/libya-uprising-and-its-aftermath

We have examined the various forms of intervention, including military intervention, economic intervention, and diplomatic intervention, and how they are used by great powers to exert their influence and achieve their strategic objectives. We have also delved into the ethical considerations surrounding the use of force, and the potential consequences of intervention for both the intervening power and the target country.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of understanding the motivations and objectives of the intervening power. As we have seen, great powers often intervene in the affairs of other countries for a variety of reasons, including protecting their economic interests, promoting their ideology, or advancing their strategic goals. However, these motivations are not always clear or transparent, and can often lead to unintended consequences and conflicts.

Another important aspect of external intervention is the role of international law and norms. While these can provide a framework for intervention, they are often subject to interpretation and can be used to justify a wide range of actions. This can lead to conflicts between intervening powers and the target country, as well as between different intervening powers.

In conclusion, external intervention and the use of force are complex and multifaceted issues that require careful consideration and analysis. As we continue to study great power military intervention, it is important to keep in mind the ethical implications and potential consequences of intervention, and to strive for a comprehensive understanding of these topics.

## Chapter 4: External Intervention and the Use of Force:




### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be discussing the written work requirement for our comprehensive study on great power military intervention. As part of this study, we will be examining the various aspects of military intervention by great powers, including the reasons behind such interventions, the methods used, and the consequences that follow.

The written work requirement for this chapter is designed to ensure that we provide a thorough and comprehensive analysis of the topic. It will involve a detailed examination of the relevant literature, as well as the collection and analysis of data on past interventions by great powers. This will include both historical interventions and more recent ones, in order to provide a well-rounded understanding of the topic.

The written work requirement will also involve the use of mathematical equations and models, where appropriate, to help us analyze and understand the complex dynamics of military intervention. This will include the use of equations such as `$y_j(n)$` and `$$\Delta w = ...$$`, which will be rendered using the popular MathJax library.

Overall, the written work requirement for this chapter is designed to ensure that we provide a comprehensive and rigorous analysis of great power military intervention. It will involve a significant amount of research and writing, but will ultimately contribute to a deeper understanding of this important topic. 





### Section: 4.1 Class Paper:

### Subsection (optional): 4.1a Paper Guidelines

In this section, we will discuss the guidelines for writing the class paper for this course. The class paper is a crucial component of this course, as it allows students to delve deeper into a specific topic related to great power military intervention and present their findings and analysis.

#### Paper Format and Submission

The class paper should follow the guidelines outlined in the appendix of "A Manual for Writers of Research Papers, Theses, and Dissertations". This includes recommendations on paper and margin sizes, options for typeface, spacing and indentation of text, pagination, and the use of titles. It is important to note that these guidelines may be supplemented or overruled by the conventions of specific disciplines or the preferences of particular institutions, departments, or instructors.

The paper should be submitted electronically and as a hard copy. The electronic submission should be in a format that is easily accessible, such as a PDF or Word document. The hard copy should be bound and include a title page with the author's name, course number and title, and date of submission.

#### Paper Topics

Students are encouraged to choose a topic related to great power military intervention that interests them and aligns with their academic and career goals. This could include a specific case study, theoretical analysis, or comparison of different interventions. The topic should be narrow enough to allow for a thorough analysis, but broad enough to contribute to the overall understanding of great power military intervention.

#### Paper Length

The class paper should be approximately 20-25 pages in length, excluding the bibliography. This length is meant to provide a balance between depth of analysis and manageability for the student. If a longer paper is necessary, students should discuss it with the instructor.

#### Paper Structure

The paper should follow a standard structure, including an introduction, literature review, methodology, analysis, and conclusion. The introduction should provide an overview of the topic and its relevance to great power military intervention. The literature review should summarize and critically analyze relevant literature on the topic. The methodology should outline the research design and data collection methods used. The analysis should present the findings and analysis of the topic. The conclusion should summarize the main points and offer recommendations for future research.

#### Paper Grading

The class paper will be graded based on the following criteria: content (50%), analysis (30%), writing style (10%), and formatting (10%). Content refers to the depth and breadth of the topic, as well as the relevance to great power military intervention. Analysis refers to the quality of the research design, data collection methods, and analysis of the topic. Writing style refers to the clarity, organization, and proper use of citations. Formatting refers to the adherence to the guidelines outlined in the appendix of "A Manual for Writers of Research Papers, Theses, and Dissertations".

#### Paper Deadline

The class paper is due at the end of the semester. Students are encouraged to start working on the paper early in the semester to ensure they have enough time to complete it. Any extensions or late submissions should be discussed with the instructor.

#### Paper Revision

Students are encouraged to revise their paper based on feedback from the instructor. This will allow for a more polished and comprehensive paper. The revised paper should be submitted by the designated deadline.

#### Paper Presentation

Students may be asked to present their paper to the class. This will provide an opportunity for students to share their findings and analysis with their peers and receive feedback. The presentation should be approximately 15-20 minutes long and should include a visual aid, such as a PowerPoint or Prezi.

#### Paper Publication

Students may have the opportunity to have their paper published in a journal or book. This will depend on the quality of the paper and the approval of the instructor. Students should discuss this with the instructor if they are interested in pursuing this option.

#### Paper Plagiarism

Plagiarism will not be tolerated in this course. All work should be original and properly cited. Any instances of plagiarism will be dealt with according to MIT's academic integrity policies.

#### Paper Resources

Students may use outside resources, such as books, articles, and websites, to aid in their research. However, all sources must be properly cited using the citation style outlined in the appendix of "A Manual for Writers of Research Papers, Theses, and Dissertations". Any direct quotes or paraphrased information should be clearly cited.

#### Paper Feedback

Students are encouraged to seek feedback from the instructor throughout the writing process. This can be done through office hours, email, or by scheduling a meeting. The instructor is available to provide guidance and support throughout the writing process.

#### Paper Grading

The class paper will be graded based on the following criteria: content (50%), analysis (30%), writing style (10%), and formatting (10%). Content refers to the depth and breadth of the topic, as well as the relevance to great power military intervention. Analysis refers to the quality of the research design, data collection methods, and analysis of the topic. Writing style refers to the clarity, organization, and proper use of citations. Formatting refers to the adherence to the guidelines outlined in the appendix of "A Manual for Writers of Research Papers, Theses, and Dissertations".





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the written work requirement for our comprehensive study on great power military intervention. We have discussed the importance of written work in this field, as it allows for a thorough and organized analysis of complex topics. We have also outlined the guidelines for writing the class paper, including formatting, submission, and topic selection. By following these guidelines and completing the written work requirement, students will be able to contribute to the overall understanding of great power military intervention and develop important skills for their academic and career paths.

### Exercises

#### Exercise 1
Choose a specific case study of great power military intervention and write a brief summary of the event. Include key details such as the involved countries, the reason for intervention, and the outcome.

#### Exercise 2
Research and analyze a theoretical aspect of great power military intervention. This could include examining the role of international law, the impact of media coverage, or the effectiveness of different intervention strategies.

#### Exercise 3
Compare and contrast two different interventions by great powers. Discuss the similarities and differences in their approaches, outcomes, and implications.

#### Exercise 4
Write a critical analysis of a recent news article related to great power military intervention. Discuss the accuracy of the information presented and any potential biases or perspectives.

#### Exercise 5
Choose a topic related to great power military intervention that interests you and write a short essay discussing your thoughts and opinions on the topic. Support your arguments with evidence and examples.


## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be discussing the topic of great power military intervention and its impact on international relations. Military intervention is a controversial and complex issue that has been a major concern for policymakers and scholars alike. It involves the use of military force by one country to intervene in the affairs of another country, often with the intention of achieving a specific political, economic, or humanitarian goal. Great powers, also known as major powers, are countries that possess significant economic, political, and military influence on a global scale. Their actions and decisions have a significant impact on the international community, making their military interventions a topic of great interest and importance.

This chapter will provide a comprehensive study of great power military intervention, examining its historical context, motivations, and consequences. We will explore the various factors that influence a great power's decision to intervene in another country, including economic interests, security concerns, and humanitarian considerations. We will also examine the different forms of military intervention, such as direct military intervention, indirect support for rebel groups, and humanitarian interventions.

Furthermore, we will delve into the impact of great power military intervention on international relations. We will discuss the effects on the intervening country, the intervened country, and the international community as a whole. We will also explore the legal and ethical implications of military intervention, including the role of international law and the responsibility to protect (R2P) doctrine.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of great power military intervention and its role in shaping international relations. By examining historical examples and current events, we will gain insight into the complexities and consequences of military intervention and its impact on global politics. 


## Chapter 5: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study




### Subsection: 4.1c Research and Writing Tips

In this section, we will provide some tips and strategies for conducting research and writing your class paper on great power military intervention. As this is a complex and multifaceted topic, it is important to approach it with a systematic and organized mindset.

#### Research Tips

1. Start early and plan ahead: Great power military intervention is a vast and complex topic, so it is important to give yourself enough time to conduct thorough research. Start early and create a timeline for yourself to ensure that you are able to complete your paper within the given deadline.

2. Use a variety of sources: In order to provide a comprehensive analysis, it is important to use a variety of sources. This could include academic articles, books, news articles, and government reports. Make sure to critically evaluate your sources and only use reliable and credible information.

3. Take detailed notes: As you conduct research, make sure to take detailed notes on key points, arguments, and evidence. This will not only help you keep track of your research, but also make it easier to organize and write your paper.

4. Analyze and critically evaluate your sources: It is important to not just gather information, but also to critically analyze and evaluate it. Consider the author's biases, the credibility of the source, and the relevance of the information to your paper.

#### Writing Tips

1. Start with an outline: Before you start writing, create an outline of your paper. This will help you organize your thoughts and ensure that you cover all necessary points.

2. Use proper formatting: Make sure to follow the guidelines provided in the written work requirement section. This includes proper citation and referencing, as well as formatting guidelines for headings, citations, and references.

3. Use clear and concise language: Avoid using overly complex language and try to keep your paper concise and easy to read. Use examples and real-world examples to illustrate your points.

4. Edit and proofread your paper: Before submitting your paper, make sure to edit and proofread it carefully. This includes checking for spelling and grammar errors, as well as ensuring that your arguments are well-supported and your paper is well-organized.

By following these tips and strategies, you can effectively conduct research and write a well-researched and well-written paper on great power military intervention. Good luck!

### Section: 4.2 Review Essays:

In this section, we will be discussing the importance of review essays in the study of great power military intervention. #### 4.2a Essay Guidelines

Before we delve into the specifics of review essays, it is important to understand the guidelines for writing them. As mentioned in the previous section, proper formatting is crucial in academic writing. In the case of review essays, it is important to follow the guidelines provided in the written work requirement section. This includes proper citation and referencing, as well as formatting guidelines for headings, citations, and references.

In addition to these guidelines, it is important to keep in mind the following tips for writing effective review essays:

1. Start early and plan ahead: As with any academic writing, it is important to start early and plan ahead when writing a review essay. This will give you enough time to conduct thorough research and critically evaluate the existing literature.

2. Use a variety of sources: In order to provide a comprehensive analysis, it is important to use a variety of sources. This could include academic articles, books, news articles, and government reports. Make sure to critically evaluate your sources and only use reliable and credible information.

3. Take detailed notes: As you conduct research, make sure to take detailed notes on key points, arguments, and evidence. This will not only help you keep track of your research, but also make it easier to organize and write your essay.

4. Analyze and critically evaluate your sources: It is important to not just gather information, but also to critically analyze and evaluate it. Consider the author's biases, the credibility of the source, and the relevance of the information to your essay.

5. Use proper formatting: In addition to the guidelines provided in the written work requirement section, it is important to use proper formatting throughout your essay. This includes using proper headings, citations, and references, as well as using clear and concise language.

By following these guidelines and tips, you can write an effective and well-researched review essay on great power military intervention. In the next section, we will discuss the specifics of writing a review essay, including how to critically evaluate existing literature and present your own arguments and insights.


#### 4.2b Essay Requirements

In addition to the general guidelines for writing review essays, there are specific requirements that must be met when writing a review essay on great power military intervention. These requirements are in place to ensure that the essay is well-researched, well-written, and contributes to the existing body of knowledge on the topic.

1. Scope and Focus: The essay must have a clear scope and focus. This means that it should cover a specific aspect of great power military intervention and provide a comprehensive analysis of that aspect. It should also have a clear thesis statement that outlines the main argument or argument being made.

2. Evidence and Analysis: The essay must be supported by evidence and analysis. This means that the author must provide evidence from reliable sources to support their arguments and must also critically analyze that evidence to draw meaningful conclusions. The analysis should also consider alternative perspectives and critically evaluate the strengths and weaknesses of different arguments.

3. Original Contribution: The essay must make an original contribution to the existing body of knowledge on great power military intervention. This could be in the form of a new argument, a new analysis of existing data, or a new perspective on the topic. It is important for the author to clearly explain how their essay contributes to the existing body of knowledge.

4. Proper Formatting: The essay must adhere to proper formatting guidelines. This includes proper citation and referencing, as well as formatting guidelines for headings, citations, and references. It is important for the author to follow these guidelines to ensure that their essay is well-organized and easy to read.

5. Length: The essay must be a minimum of 10 pages in length. This allows for a more in-depth analysis and discussion of the topic. However, the author should aim to be concise and only include information that is relevant to their argument.

6. Submission Deadline: The essay must be submitted by the designated deadline. Late submissions will not be accepted unless there is a valid excuse and prior arrangement with the instructor.

By meeting these requirements, the author can ensure that their review essay is well-researched, well-written, and contributes to the existing body of knowledge on great power military intervention. It is important for the author to carefully consider these requirements and to seek guidance from the instructor if needed.


#### 4.2c Essay Grading

In this section, we will discuss the grading criteria for review essays on great power military intervention. It is important for students to understand how their essays will be evaluated in order to ensure that they meet the necessary requirements and expectations.

1. Content: The essay will be graded on the depth and breadth of content covered. This includes the scope and focus of the essay, as well as the level of detail and analysis provided. The essay should cover a specific aspect of great power military intervention and provide a comprehensive analysis. It should also have a clear thesis statement that outlines the main argument or argument being made.

2. Evidence and Analysis: The essay will be graded on the quality and quantity of evidence used to support arguments. This includes the reliability of sources and the depth of analysis provided. The author must critically analyze evidence to draw meaningful conclusions and also consider alternative perspectives. The essay should also critically evaluate the strengths and weaknesses of different arguments.

3. Original Contribution: The essay will be graded on the originality of its contribution to the existing body of knowledge on great power military intervention. This could be in the form of a new argument, a new analysis of existing data, or a new perspective on the topic. The author must clearly explain how their essay contributes to the existing body of knowledge.

4. Proper Formatting: The essay will be graded on its adherence to proper formatting guidelines. This includes proper citation and referencing, as well as formatting guidelines for headings, citations, and references. It is important for the author to follow these guidelines to ensure that their essay is well-organized and easy to read.

5. Length: The essay will be graded on its length and conciseness. While a minimum of 10 pages is required, the author should aim to be concise and only include information that is relevant to their argument. The essay should also be well-structured and easy to follow.

6. Submission Deadline: The essay will be graded on its timeliness. Late submissions will not be accepted unless there is a valid excuse and prior arrangement with the instructor. It is important for students to submit their essays on time to ensure that they receive a fair grade.

By understanding these grading criteria, students can ensure that their essays meet the necessary requirements and expectations. It is important for students to carefully consider these criteria when writing their essays to ensure that they receive a high grade.

## Chapter 5: Research Methods:




### Section: 4.2 Review Essays:

In this section, we will be discussing the importance of review essays in the study of great power military intervention. Review essays are a crucial component of academic writing, as they provide a critical analysis and evaluation of existing literature on a particular topic. In the context of great power military intervention, review essays play a vital role in helping us understand the complexities and nuances of this phenomenon.

#### 4.2a Essay Guidelines

Before we delve into the specifics of review essays, it is important to understand the guidelines for writing them. As mentioned in the previous section, proper formatting is crucial in academic writing. In the case of review essays, it is important to follow the guidelines provided in the written work requirement section. This includes proper citation and referencing, as well as formatting guidelines for headings, citations, and references.

In addition to these guidelines, it is important to keep in mind the following tips for writing effective review essays:

1. Start early and plan ahead: As with any academic writing, it is important to start early and plan ahead when writing a review essay. This will give you enough time to conduct thorough research and critically evaluate the existing literature.

2. Use a variety of sources: In order to provide a comprehensive analysis, it is important to use a variety of sources. This could include academic articles, books, news articles, and government reports. Make sure to critically evaluate your sources and only use reliable and credible information.

3. Take detailed notes: As you conduct research, make sure to take detailed notes on key points, arguments, and evidence. This will not only help you keep track of your research, but also make it easier to organize and write your essay.

4. Analyze and critically evaluate your sources: It is important to not just gather information, but also to critically analyze and evaluate it. This involves considering the author's biases, the credibility of the sources used, and the overall arguments presented.

5. Organize your essay: A well-organized essay is crucial in effectively communicating your ideas and arguments. Make sure to create an outline before you start writing, and use headings and subheadings to guide your readers through your essay.

6. Use proper citations and references: As mentioned earlier, proper citation and referencing are essential in academic writing. Make sure to follow the guidelines provided in the written work requirement section and use a consistent citation style throughout your essay.

7. Edit and proofread your essay: Before submitting your essay, make sure to edit and proofread it carefully. This includes checking for spelling and grammar errors, as well as ensuring that your arguments are well-supported and your essay is well-written.

By following these guidelines and tips, you can write a comprehensive and effective review essay on great power military intervention. Remember to always critically evaluate your sources and present a well-supported and well-written argument.

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, the use of military force has become a common occurrence in international relations. Great powers, such as the United States, Russia, and China, have been involved in various military interventions around the world. These interventions have been met with both support and criticism from the international community. In this chapter, we will delve into the topic of great power military intervention and explore its various aspects.

We will begin by defining what military intervention is and its different forms. We will then examine the historical context of great power military intervention, including its origins and evolution over time. Next, we will discuss the motivations behind great power military intervention, such as economic, political, and humanitarian reasons. We will also explore the impact of these interventions on the countries involved, both in terms of their political and economic stability.

Furthermore, we will analyze the effectiveness of great power military intervention in achieving its intended goals. This will include a discussion on the successes and failures of past interventions, as well as the lessons learned from them. We will also examine the role of international organizations, such as the United Nations, in regulating and overseeing these interventions.

Finally, we will discuss the future of great power military intervention and its potential impact on global politics. This will include a discussion on the changing nature of military interventions and the role of emerging powers, such as India and Brazil, in this field. We will also explore the ethical considerations surrounding great power military intervention and the need for a more responsible and accountable approach.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive study of great power military intervention, shedding light on its complexities and implications. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the role of great powers in international conflicts and the impact of their military interventions on global politics.

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be discussing the topic of great power military intervention and its impact on the international community. Great power military intervention refers to the use of military force by a powerful nation to intervene in the affairs of another country. This can take various forms, such as direct military intervention, indirect support for rebel groups, or economic sanctions. The impact of great power military intervention can be seen in the political, economic, and social aspects of the affected country.

The study of great power military intervention is crucial in understanding the dynamics of international relations. It allows us to examine the motivations and strategies of powerful nations in their interactions with other countries. By studying the historical and contemporary examples of great power military intervention, we can gain insights into the complexities of international politics and the role of military force in shaping global affairs.

In this chapter, we will explore the various aspects of great power military intervention, including its historical context, motivations, and consequences. We will also examine the different types of interventions and their impact on the affected countries. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of great power military intervention and its role in shaping the international community.
