## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be discussing the topic of great power military intervention and its impact on international relations. Military intervention is a controversial and complex issue that has been a major concern for policymakers and scholars alike. It involves the use of military force by one country to intervene in the affairs of another country, often with the intention of achieving a specific political or strategic objective. Great powers, also known as major powers, are countries that possess significant economic, political, and military influence on a global scale. Their actions and decisions have a significant impact on international relations and can shape the course of events in the international arena.

The study of great power military intervention is crucial for understanding the dynamics of international relations. It sheds light on the motivations and strategies of major powers, as well as the consequences of their actions. This chapter will provide a comprehensive study of great power military intervention, covering various aspects such as the historical context, motivations, methods, and outcomes of intervention. We will also examine the role of international law and organizations in regulating and overseeing military intervention.

The chapter will be divided into several sections, each focusing on a specific aspect of great power military intervention. We will begin by providing an overview of the topic and its significance in international relations. Then, we will delve into the historical context of military intervention, examining its evolution over time and the factors that have influenced its use. Next, we will explore the motivations behind great power military intervention, including economic, political, and humanitarian factors. We will also discuss the methods used by major powers to intervene in the affairs of other countries, such as direct military intervention, economic sanctions, and diplomatic pressure.

Furthermore, we will examine the outcomes of great power military intervention, including its effectiveness in achieving the intended objectives and its impact on the stability and security of the intervened country. We will also discuss the role of international law and organizations in regulating and overseeing military intervention, including the principles of sovereignty and non-intervention. Finally, we will conclude with a discussion on the future of great power military intervention and its implications for international relations.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of great power military intervention and its impact on international relations. By examining the historical context, motivations, methods, and outcomes of intervention, we hope to shed light on the complexities of this issue and its significance in the global arena.

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In this chapter, we will be discussing the topic of great power military intervention and its impact on international relations. Military intervention is a controversial and complex issue that has been a major concern for policymakers and scholars alike. It involves the use of military force by one country to intervene in the affairs of another country, often with the intention of achieving a specific political or strategic objective. Great powers, also known as major powers, are countries that possess significant economic, political, and military influence on a global scale. Their actions and decisions have a significant impact on international relations and can shape the course of events in the international arena.

The study of great power military intervention is crucial for understanding the dynamics of international relations. It sheds light on the motivations and strategies of major powers, as well as the consequences of their actions. This chapter will provide a comprehensive study of great power military intervention, covering various aspects such as the historical context, motivations, methods, and outcomes of intervention. We will also examine the role of international law and organizations in regulating and overseeing military intervention.

The chapter will be divided into several sections, each focusing on a specific aspect of great power military intervention. We will begin by providing an overview of the topic and its significance in international relations. Then, we will delve into the historical context of military intervention, examining its evolution over time and the factors that have influenced its use. Next, we will explore the motivations behind great power military intervention, including economic, political, and humanitarian factors. We will also discuss the methods used by major powers to intervene in the affairs of other countries, such as direct military intervention, economic sanctions, and diplomatic pressure.

Furthermore, we will examine the outcomes of great power military intervention, including its effectiveness in achieving the intended objectives and its impact on the stability and security of the intervened country. We will also discuss the role of international law and organizations in regulating and overseeing military intervention, including the principles of sovereignty and non-intervention. Finally, we will conclude with a discussion on the future of great power military intervention and its implications for international relations.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of great power military intervention and its impact on international relations. By examining the historical context, motivations, methods, and outcomes of intervention, we hope to shed light on the complexities of this issue and its significance in the global arena. 


## Chapter 8: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study




### Introduction

The use of military intervention by great powers has been a topic of great debate and controversy throughout history. It is a complex issue that involves ethical considerations, political motivations, and the potential for both positive and negative outcomes. In this chapter, we will delve into the ethics of intervention, examining the various ethical frameworks and principles that guide the decision-making process of great powers when it comes to military intervention.

We will begin by defining what intervention is and the different types of intervention that can be used by great powers. We will then explore the ethical considerations that come into play when deciding whether to intervene in a conflict or not. This will include examining the principles of just war theory, which provides a framework for evaluating the morality of intervention.

Next, we will discuss the role of international law in guiding the ethics of intervention. This will involve examining the principles of international law, such as the principle of non-intervention, and how they are applied in practice. We will also explore the role of international organizations, such as the United Nations, in regulating and overseeing intervention by great powers.

Finally, we will examine case studies of past interventions by great powers, such as the United States' intervention in Iraq and Russia's intervention in Syria. These case studies will provide real-world examples to illustrate the ethical dilemmas and challenges faced by great powers when deciding whether to intervene in a conflict.

By the end of this chapter, readers will have a comprehensive understanding of the ethics of intervention and the complex factors that influence the decision-making process of great powers. This knowledge will be essential in understanding the role of military intervention in shaping global conflicts and power dynamics.




### Subsection: 8.1a Humanitarian Intervention

Humanitarian intervention is a form of intervention that is aimed at protecting civilians from violence and human rights abuses. It is often seen as a last resort when other diplomatic efforts have failed to address the situation. In this subsection, we will explore the concept of humanitarian intervention and its ethical implications.

#### The Concept of Humanitarian Intervention

Humanitarian intervention is a complex and controversial topic that has been debated by scholars and policymakers for decades. It is often seen as a form of intervention that is justified by humanitarian concerns, rather than political or strategic interests. However, the line between humanitarian intervention and other forms of intervention can be blurred, and there are often competing interests at play.

One of the key debates surrounding humanitarian intervention is the concept of responsibility to protect (R2P). R2P is a principle that was first introduced in 2005 and has since been used to justify interventions in Libya, Syria, and other countries. It states that states have a responsibility to protect their citizens from violence and human rights abuses, and if they are unable or unwilling to do so, other states have a responsibility to intervene.

#### Ethical Considerations of Humanitarian Intervention

The ethics of humanitarian intervention are complex and multifaceted. On one hand, there is a moral obligation to protect innocent civilians from violence and human rights abuses. On the other hand, there are concerns about the potential negative consequences of intervention, such as the loss of lives and resources, as well as the potential for unintended consequences.

One ethical framework that has been used to evaluate humanitarian intervention is just war theory. Just war theory provides a set of principles for determining the morality of a war or intervention. These principles include the just cause principle, which states that intervention must be motivated by a just cause, such as protecting innocent civilians. Other principles include the proportionality principle, which states that the harm caused by intervention must not outweigh the potential benefits, and the last resort principle, which states that intervention should only be used as a last resort after all other diplomatic efforts have failed.

#### The Role of International Law in Humanitarian Intervention

International law plays a crucial role in regulating humanitarian intervention. The United Nations Charter, in particular, has been used to justify interventions in cases of genocide, war crimes, and other human rights violations. However, there are also limitations and controversies surrounding the use of international law in humanitarian intervention.

One limitation is the lack of a clear legal framework for humanitarian intervention. The UN Charter does not specifically mention humanitarian intervention, and there is no international law that explicitly allows for it. This has led to debates over the legality of certain interventions and the interpretation of international law.

Another controversy is the role of the Security Council in authorizing interventions. The Security Council has the power to authorize interventions under Chapter VII of the UN Charter, but there have been instances where the Council has failed to act in cases of humanitarian crises. This has raised questions about the effectiveness of international law in protecting civilians.

#### Conclusion

In conclusion, humanitarian intervention is a complex and controversial topic that requires careful consideration of ethical and legal principles. While there is a moral obligation to protect innocent civilians, there are also concerns about the potential negative consequences of intervention. International law plays a crucial role in regulating humanitarian intervention, but there are also limitations and controversies surrounding its application. As great powers continue to intervene in conflicts around the world, it is important to carefully evaluate the ethical implications of these interventions and strive for a more just and equitable approach to protecting civilians.





### Subsection: 8.1b Just War Theory

Just war theory is a philosophical framework that has been used to evaluate the morality of war and intervention. It originated in ancient Greece and Rome, and has been further developed by Christian thinkers such as Augustine of Hippo. Just war theory provides a set of principles for determining the morality of a war or intervention, and has been used to justify humanitarian intervention in certain cases.

#### The Principles of Just War Theory

Just war theory is based on the principle of jus ad bellum, which refers to the justification for going to war. This principle states that a war can only be justified if it is fought for a just cause, with a just intention, and with a reasonable chance of success. The just cause principle requires that the war be fought for a legitimate reason, such as self-defense or the protection of innocent civilians. The just intention principle states that the war must be fought with the intention of restoring peace and justice, rather than for personal or political gain. The reasonable chance of success principle requires that there be a realistic chance of achieving the just cause and intention.

#### The Ethics of Humanitarian Intervention

Just war theory has been used to justify humanitarian intervention in cases where there is a clear and present danger to innocent civilians. In these cases, the principle of jus ad bellum can be applied to determine if the intervention is justified. If the intervention meets the criteria of a just cause, just intention, and reasonable chance of success, then it can be considered a just war.

However, just war theory also recognizes the potential for unintended consequences and the need for proportionality in the use of force. This means that even if a war meets the criteria of jus ad bellum, it may still be unjust if the potential consequences are disproportionate to the just cause. This principle has been used to criticize certain interventions, such as the invasion of Iraq in 2003, which was seen as disproportionate to the just cause of removing weapons of mass destruction.

#### Conclusion

Just war theory provides a useful framework for evaluating the ethics of humanitarian intervention. While it is not without its flaws and limitations, it provides a set of principles that can help guide decision-making in complex and difficult situations. As such, it remains an important tool for understanding and evaluating the ethics of intervention.





### Subsection: 8.1c Responsibility to Protect

The Responsibility to Protect (R2P) is a principle that was first introduced in 2005 at the United Nations World Summit. It is a response to the failure of the international community to intervene in the Rwandan genocide of 1994, and is a recognition of the responsibility of states to protect their citizens from mass atrocities. The principle is based on the idea that sovereignty is not an absolute right, and that the international community has a responsibility to protect human rights and prevent genocide, war crimes, ethnic cleansing, and crimes against humanity.

#### The Three Pillars of R2P

The Responsibility to Protect consists of three important and mutually-reinforcing pillars, as articulated in the 2009 Report of the Secretary-General on the issue. These pillars are:

1. The responsibility of states to protect their citizens from mass atrocities.
2. The responsibility of the international community to assist states in meeting their responsibility to protect.
3. The responsibility of the international community to take collective action, in accordance with the Charter of the United Nations, when a state is unable or unwilling to protect its citizens from mass atrocities.

These pillars build off the principles of sovereignty, non-intervention, and the responsibility to protect, as outlined in the 2005 World Summit Outcome Document. The principle of sovereignty is recognized, but is not absolute. The principle of non-intervention is also recognized, but is not absolute. The principle of the responsibility to protect is emphasized, and is seen as a way to strengthen sovereignty, not weaken it.

#### The Responsibility to Protect and Humanitarian Intervention

The Responsibility to Protect differs from humanitarian intervention in four important ways. First, humanitarian intervention only refers to the use of military force, whereas R2P is first and foremost a preventive principle that emphasizes a range of measures to stem the risk of genocide, war crimes, ethnic cleansing or crimes against humanity before the crimes are threatened or occur. The use of force may only be carried out as a measure of last resort, when all other non-coercive measures have failed, and only when it is authorized by the United Nations Security Council.

Second, humanitarian intervention is often seen as a unilateral action, while R2P is a collective responsibility of the international community. This means that the responsibility to protect is not just the responsibility of one state, but of the entire international community.

Third, humanitarian intervention is often seen as a last resort, while R2P is seen as a preventive measure. This means that the responsibility to protect is not just about responding to mass atrocities, but also about preventing them from occurring in the first place.

Finally, humanitarian intervention is often seen as a temporary measure, while R2P is seen as a long-term commitment. This means that the responsibility to protect is not just about intervening in a crisis, but also about helping states to build their capacity to protect their citizens in the long term.

In conclusion, the Responsibility to Protect is a crucial principle in the ethics of intervention. It recognizes the responsibility of states to protect their citizens from mass atrocities, the responsibility of the international community to assist states in meeting this responsibility, and the responsibility of the international community to take collective action when a state is unable or unwilling to protect its citizens. It also emphasizes the importance of preventive measures, collective responsibility, and long-term commitment in the ethics of intervention. 





### Subsection: 8.2a Sovereignty vs. Human Rights

The concept of sovereignty has been a cornerstone of international law and relations for centuries. It is the principle that a state has the right to govern itself without external interference. However, with the rise of human rights as a global concern, the concept of sovereignty has come under scrutiny. The question of whether a state's sovereignty should take precedence over human rights has been a contentious issue in the realm of intervention.

#### Sovereignty as a Legal Concept

Sovereignty, as a legal concept, is often categorized into two types: de jure and de facto. De jure sovereignty refers to the legal right to exercise control over a territory. This is typically established through international recognition and agreements. De facto sovereignty, on the other hand, refers to the practical exercise of control over a territory, regardless of any legal recognition. This can be seen in situations where a state may not have formal recognition, but is able to exert control over a territory.

#### Sovereignty and Independence

The concept of sovereignty is often intertwined with the concept of independence. However, it is important to note that sovereignty can be transferred as a legal right, while independence cannot. A state can achieve de facto independence long after acquiring sovereignty, as seen in the cases of Cambodia, Laos, and Vietnam. Additionally, independence can be suspended when an entire region becomes subject to an occupation, as seen in the case of Iraq in the Iraq War of 2003.

#### Sovereignty and Human Rights

The concept of sovereignty has been a major factor in the debate over intervention. The principle of non-intervention, which is often seen as a manifestation of sovereignty, has been used to justify inaction in the face of human rights abuses. However, the principle of the responsibility to protect, as outlined in the Responsibility to Protect (R2P), recognizes that sovereignty is not an absolute right and that the international community has a responsibility to protect human rights.

#### Sovereignty and the Responsibility to Protect

The R2P principle builds off the principles of sovereignty, non-intervention, and the responsibility to protect, as outlined in the 2005 World Summit Outcome Document. It recognizes that sovereignty is not an absolute right and that the international community has a responsibility to protect human rights. The R2P principle also emphasizes the responsibility of states to protect their citizens from mass atrocities, the responsibility of the international community to assist states in meeting this responsibility, and the responsibility of the international community to take collective action when a state is unable or unwilling to protect its citizens.

#### Sovereignty and Humanitarian Intervention

The R2P principle differs from humanitarian intervention in four important ways. First, humanitarian intervention only refers to the use of military force, while R2P is a preventive principle that emphasizes a range of measures to protect human rights. Second, humanitarian intervention is often seen as a last resort, while R2P emphasizes the importance of prevention and early intervention. Third, humanitarian intervention is often seen as a unilateral action, while R2P emphasizes the importance of collective action and international cooperation. Finally, humanitarian intervention is often seen as a temporary measure, while R2P emphasizes the importance of long-term solutions to address the root causes of human rights abuses.

In conclusion, the concept of sovereignty has been a major factor in the debate over intervention. While it is important to respect a state's sovereignty, it is also important to recognize that sovereignty is not an absolute right and that the international community has a responsibility to protect human rights. The R2P principle provides a framework for balancing these competing interests and for addressing the ethical dilemmas that arise in the realm of intervention.




### Subsection: 8.2b Selectivity of Intervention

The selectivity of intervention is a crucial ethical consideration in the use of military force. It refers to the decision of whether to intervene in a particular situation, and if so, how extensively. This decision is often influenced by a variety of factors, including the nature of the conflict, the potential consequences of intervention, and the interests of the intervening state.

#### The Ethics of Selectivity

The selectivity of intervention raises a number of ethical questions. One of the most fundamental is whether it is ever ethical to intervene in the affairs of another state. This question is often tied to the concept of sovereignty, as discussed in the previous section. The principle of non-intervention, which is often seen as a manifestation of sovereignty, has been used to justify inaction in the face of human rights abuses. However, the principle of the responsibility to protect, as outlined in the Responsibility to Protect (R2P), recognizes that sovereignty is not an absolute right, and that states have a responsibility to protect their citizens from mass atrocities.

Another important ethical consideration is the selectivity of intervention. This refers to the decision of whether to intervene in a particular situation, and if so, how extensively. This decision is often influenced by a variety of factors, including the nature of the conflict, the potential consequences of intervention, and the interests of the intervening state. For example, a state may choose to intervene in a conflict that directly affects its own interests, but not in a conflict that does not directly impact it. This selectivity can raise questions about fairness and consistency, as well as about the effectiveness of intervention.

#### The Ethics of Selectivity in Practice

The ethics of selectivity in intervention can be seen in a variety of historical and contemporary cases. For example, the United States' intervention in Iraq in 2003 has been criticized for its selectivity, as it was seen as being motivated primarily by the US's own interests, rather than a genuine concern for the welfare of the Iraqi people. On the other hand, the US's intervention in Libya in 2011, under the auspices of the R2P, has been seen as a more ethical example of selectivity, as it was motivated by a genuine concern for the protection of civilians.

In conclusion, the selectivity of intervention is a complex ethical issue that requires careful consideration. It involves a balance between the principles of non-intervention and the responsibility to protect, as well as a consideration of the interests of the intervening state. It is a crucial aspect of the ethics of intervention, and one that will continue to be debated in the future.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have delved into the complex and often contentious topic of the ethics of intervention by great powers. We have explored the various ethical frameworks that can be used to evaluate such interventions, including utilitarianism, deontology, and virtue ethics. We have also examined the role of international law and the responsibility to protect in guiding these interventions.

The chapter has highlighted the importance of considering the ethical implications of intervention, both for the intervening power and for the target of the intervention. It has underscored the need for a careful and nuanced approach, taking into account the potential consequences of intervention, the legitimacy of the intervention, and the ethical principles that guide the intervention.

The chapter has also emphasized the importance of transparency and accountability in the conduct of interventions. It has argued that these are not only ethical considerations, but also contribute to the effectiveness and legitimacy of interventions.

In conclusion, the ethics of intervention is a complex and multifaceted topic that requires careful consideration and a commitment to ethical principles. It is a topic that will continue to be of great importance in the future, as great powers continue to intervene in the affairs of other states.

### Subsection: 8.2c Unintended Consequences

The concept of unintended consequences is a crucial aspect of the ethics of intervention. Unintended consequences refer to the unforeseen and often undesirable outcomes that can result from military intervention. These consequences can range from the loss of civilian lives to the exacerbation of existing conflicts.

#### The Ethics of Unintended Consequences

The ethics of unintended consequences in intervention are complex and multifaceted. On one hand, it can be argued that the potential for unintended consequences should not deter intervention in cases where human rights are being violated or where there is a clear and present danger to international peace and security. The responsibility to protect, as outlined in the Responsibility to Protect (R2P), recognizes this principle.

On the other hand, the potential for unintended consequences should also be a major consideration in the decision to intervene. This is because unintended consequences can often be difficult to predict and can lead to further harm and instability. Therefore, it is important for states to carefully consider the potential unintended consequences of intervention before deciding to intervene.

#### Unintended Consequences in Practice

The concept of unintended consequences can be seen in a variety of historical and contemporary cases. For example, the United States' intervention in Iraq in 2003 was intended to remove Saddam Hussein's regime and promote democracy in the region. However, the intervention resulted in a prolonged and costly occupation, the rise of sectarian violence, and the destabilization of the region. These unintended consequences have had far-reaching effects, including the rise of ISIS and the ongoing Syrian civil war.

Another example is the NATO intervention in Libya in 2011, which was intended to protect civilians from the violence of the Gaddafi regime. However, the intervention resulted in a prolonged conflict and the eventual collapse of the Gaddafi regime, leading to a power vacuum and ongoing instability in the country.

These cases highlight the importance of considering unintended consequences in the decision to intervene. They also underscore the need for careful planning and consideration of potential outcomes before intervention.




### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex and often controversial topic of the ethics of intervention by great powers. We have examined the various ethical frameworks that can be used to evaluate the morality of intervention, including utilitarianism, deontology, and virtue ethics. We have also discussed the role of international law and the responsibility to protect in shaping the ethical considerations of intervention.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is that there is no one-size-fits-all approach to evaluating the ethics of intervention. Each intervention must be examined on its own merits, taking into account the specific circumstances and consequences. However, it is important for policymakers and military leaders to have a strong understanding of these ethical frameworks and their implications in order to make informed decisions about intervention.

Another important aspect to consider is the potential unintended consequences of intervention. While intervention may be necessary in certain situations, it is crucial to carefully consider the potential long-term effects and unintended consequences. This requires a deep understanding of the cultural, political, and social dynamics at play in the intervention.

In conclusion, the ethics of intervention is a complex and multifaceted topic that requires careful consideration and evaluation. It is our hope that this chapter has provided a comprehensive overview of the key ethical considerations and frameworks that can aid in this evaluation.

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, the use of military force has become a common occurrence in international relations. Great powers, such as the United States, Russia, and China, have been involved in numerous military interventions around the world. These interventions have been met with both support and criticism from various stakeholders. In this chapter, we will delve into the topic of great power military intervention and its impact on international law.

The use of military force has been a contentious issue in international law for centuries. The Kellogg-Briand Pact of 1928, also known as the General Treaty for the Renunciation of War, was a significant step towards regulating the use of military force. This pact was signed by 62 states, including the United States and France, and aimed to prohibit the use of war as an instrument of national policy. However, despite this agreement, the use of military force has continued to be a major issue in international relations.

In this chapter, we will explore the various aspects of great power military intervention and its impact on international law. We will examine the historical context of military intervention, the legal framework surrounding it, and the role of international organizations in regulating it. Additionally, we will also discuss the ethical considerations and implications of great power military intervention.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of great power military intervention and its impact on international law. By examining the various aspects of this topic, we hope to shed light on the complex and often controversial issue of military intervention and its role in shaping the global political landscape.

## Chapter 9: Great Power Military Intervention and International Law




### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex and often controversial topic of the ethics of intervention by great powers. We have examined the various ethical frameworks that can be used to evaluate the morality of intervention, including utilitarianism, deontology, and virtue ethics. We have also discussed the role of international law and the responsibility to protect in shaping the ethical considerations of intervention.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is that there is no one-size-fits-all approach to evaluating the ethics of intervention. Each intervention must be examined on its own merits, taking into account the specific circumstances and consequences. However, it is important for policymakers and military leaders to have a strong understanding of these ethical frameworks and their implications in order to make informed decisions about intervention.

Another important aspect to consider is the potential unintended consequences of intervention. While intervention may be necessary in certain situations, it is crucial to carefully consider the potential long-term effects and unintended consequences. This requires a deep understanding of the cultural, political, and social dynamics at play in the intervention.

In conclusion, the ethics of intervention is a complex and multifaceted topic that requires careful consideration and evaluation. It is our hope that this chapter has provided a comprehensive overview of the key ethical considerations and frameworks that can aid in this evaluation.

### Exercises

#### Exercise 1
Using the ethical framework of utilitarianism, evaluate the morality of a hypothetical intervention in a foreign country. Consider the potential consequences for both the intervening country and the intervened country.

#### Exercise 2
Discuss the role of international law in shaping the ethics of intervention. Provide examples of how international law can both support and limit the use of intervention.

#### Exercise 3
Research and analyze a historical case of intervention by a great power. Using the ethical framework of deontology, evaluate the morality of the intervention and discuss any potential ethical dilemmas that may have arisen.

#### Exercise 4
Discuss the responsibility to protect (R2P) and its implications for the ethics of intervention. Consider the potential benefits and drawbacks of using R2P as a justification for intervention.

#### Exercise 5
Reflect on the importance of understanding the cultural, political, and social dynamics at play in a potential intervention. Discuss how this understanding can inform the ethical evaluation of intervention.


### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the complex and often controversial topic of the ethics of intervention by great powers. We have examined the various ethical frameworks that can be used to evaluate the morality of intervention, including utilitarianism, deontology, and virtue ethics. We have also discussed the role of international law and the responsibility to protect in shaping the ethical considerations of intervention.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is that there is no one-size-fits-all approach to evaluating the ethics of intervention. Each intervention must be examined on its own merits, taking into account the specific circumstances and consequences. However, it is important for policymakers and military leaders to have a strong understanding of these ethical frameworks and their implications in order to make informed decisions about intervention.

Another important aspect to consider is the potential unintended consequences of intervention. While intervention may be necessary in certain situations, it is crucial to carefully consider the potential long-term effects and unintended consequences. This requires a deep understanding of the cultural, political, and social dynamics at play in the intervention.

In conclusion, the ethics of intervention is a complex and multifaceted topic that requires careful consideration and evaluation. It is our hope that this chapter has provided a comprehensive overview of the key ethical considerations and frameworks that can aid in this evaluation.

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, the use of military force has become a common occurrence in international relations. Great powers, such as the United States, Russia, and China, have been involved in numerous military interventions around the world. These interventions have been met with both support and criticism from various stakeholders. In this chapter, we will delve into the topic of great power military intervention and its impact on international law.

The use of military force has been a contentious issue in international law for centuries. The Kellogg-Briand Pact of 1928, also known as the General Treaty for the Renunciation of War, was a significant step towards regulating the use of military force. This pact was signed by 62 states, including the United States and France, and aimed to prohibit the use of war as an instrument of national policy. However, despite this agreement, the use of military force has continued to be a major issue in international relations.

In this chapter, we will explore the various aspects of great power military intervention and its impact on international law. We will examine the historical context of military intervention, the legal framework surrounding it, and the role of international organizations in regulating it. Additionally, we will also discuss the ethical considerations and implications of great power military intervention.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of great power military intervention and its impact on international law. By examining the various aspects of this topic, we hope to shed light on the complex and often controversial issue of military intervention and its role in shaping the global political landscape.

### Introduction

The role of international organizations in great power military intervention is a crucial aspect that cannot be overlooked. Their involvement can range from providing humanitarian aid and diplomatic efforts to deploying military forces and enforcing peacekeeping missions.

In this chapter, we will delve into the complexities of international organizations and their role in great power military intervention. Additionally, we will examine the impact of their actions on the outcome of interventions and the long-term effects on the affected regions.

These include issues of sovereignty, lack of consensus among member states, and resource constraints. We will also explore the ethical considerations surrounding their involvement and the potential consequences of their actions.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the role of international organizations in great power military intervention. By examining their actions and impact, we can gain valuable insights into the complexities of global conflicts and the role of international cooperation in resolving them. 


# Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

## Chapter 9: The Role of International Organizations




### Introduction

The role of international organizations in great power military intervention is a crucial aspect that cannot be overlooked. These organizations, such as the United Nations, NATO, and the European Union, play a significant role in shaping the landscape of global conflicts and interventions. Their involvement can range from providing humanitarian aid and diplomatic efforts to deploying military forces and enforcing peacekeeping missions.

In this chapter, we will delve into the complexities of international organizations and their role in great power military intervention. We will explore the various factors that influence their involvement, such as political ideologies, economic interests, and humanitarian concerns. Additionally, we will examine the impact of their actions on the outcome of interventions and the long-term effects on the affected regions.

Furthermore, we will also discuss the challenges and limitations faced by international organizations in their efforts to intervene in conflicts. These include issues of sovereignty, lack of consensus among member states, and resource constraints. We will also explore the ethical considerations surrounding their involvement and the potential consequences of their actions.

Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the role of international organizations in great power military intervention. By examining their actions and impact, we can gain valuable insights into the complexities of global conflicts and the role of international cooperation in resolving them.




### Subsection: 9.1b UN Peacekeeping Missions

The United Nations has been involved in numerous peacekeeping missions since its inception in 1945. These missions are aimed at maintaining international peace and security, protecting human rights, and promoting economic and social development. The UN peacekeeping missions are carried out by the Department of Peacekeeping Operations (DPKO) and are funded by member states.

The UN peacekeeping missions are governed by the principles of consent, impartiality, and the use of minimum force. The consent of the host country is required for the deployment of UN peacekeeping forces. This is to ensure that the mission is carried out with the support and cooperation of the local population. The principle of impartiality requires UN peacekeepers to remain neutral and unbiased in their actions. This is to ensure that they are not seen as taking sides in the conflict. The use of minimum force is a crucial principle in UN peacekeeping missions. UN peacekeepers are only authorized to use force in self-defense or to protect civilians under imminent threat.

The UN peacekeeping missions have been deployed in various conflict situations around the world, including the Middle East, Africa, and the Balkans. These missions have been successful in maintaining peace and stability in many cases, but they have also faced challenges and criticisms.

One of the main challenges faced by UN peacekeeping missions is the lack of resources and support from member states. The UN relies heavily on voluntary contributions from member states for its peacekeeping operations. This can lead to unequal distribution of resources and can hinder the effectiveness of the missions.

Another challenge is the lack of clear mandate and objectives for the missions. In many cases, the UN peacekeeping missions are deployed without a clear understanding of their objectives and the means to achieve them. This can lead to confusion and ineffectiveness of the missions.

The UN peacekeeping missions have also faced criticism for their lack of accountability and human rights violations. In some cases, UN peacekeepers have been accused of sexual abuse and exploitation of local populations. This has damaged the reputation of the UN and has raised questions about the effectiveness of its peacekeeping missions.

Despite these challenges and criticisms, the UN peacekeeping missions continue to play a crucial role in maintaining international peace and security. They provide a platform for diplomatic efforts and serve as a bridge between conflicting parties. The UN peacekeeping missions also provide a means for the international community to address conflicts and promote stability in troubled regions.

In the next section, we will explore the role of international organizations in great power military intervention, specifically focusing on the United Nations. We will examine the various factors that influence their involvement, such as political ideologies, economic interests, and humanitarian concerns. Additionally, we will also discuss the impact of their actions on the outcome of interventions and the long-term effects on the affected regions.





### Subsection: 9.1c Case Studies

In this section, we will examine some case studies of UN peacekeeping missions to gain a deeper understanding of the challenges and successes faced by these missions.

#### Case Study 1: The United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon (UNIFIL)

The United Nations Interim Force in Lebanon (UNIFIL) was deployed in Lebanon in 1978 to maintain peace and stability in the region. The mission was initially deployed for a period of six months, but it has been extended multiple times due to the ongoing conflict in the region.

One of the main challenges faced by UNIFIL is the lack of support from the local population. The Lebanese government has been hesitant to provide full support to the UNIFIL forces, and the local population has been hostile towards them. This has hindered the effectiveness of the mission and has put UNIFIL forces at risk.

Another challenge faced by UNIFIL is the presence of armed groups in the region. These groups have been involved in various conflicts and have been a source of instability in the region. UNIFIL forces have been deployed to monitor and maintain peace in these areas, but their presence has been met with resistance from these groups.

Despite these challenges, UNIFIL has been successful in maintaining peace and stability in Lebanon. The mission has been able to prevent further escalation of the conflict and has helped to create a safe and secure environment for the local population.

#### Case Study 2: The United Nations Mission in the Central African Republic (MINUSCA)

The United Nations Mission in the Central African Republic (MINUSCA) was deployed in 2014 to maintain peace and stability in the country. The mission was deployed in response to the ongoing conflict and humanitarian crisis in the country.

One of the main challenges faced by MINUSCA is the lack of resources and support from the local population. The Central African Republic is one of the poorest countries in the world, and the local population has been struggling to meet their basic needs. This has made it difficult for MINUSCA to carry out its mission effectively.

Another challenge faced by MINUSCA is the presence of armed groups in the country. These groups have been involved in various conflicts and have been a source of instability in the region. MINUSCA forces have been deployed to monitor and maintain peace in these areas, but their presence has been met with resistance from these groups.

Despite these challenges, MINUSCA has been successful in maintaining peace and stability in the Central African Republic. The mission has been able to prevent further escalation of the conflict and has helped to create a safe and secure environment for the local population.

### Conclusion

These case studies highlight the challenges and successes faced by UN peacekeeping missions. The UN plays a crucial role in maintaining international peace and stability, and its peacekeeping missions are essential in achieving this goal. However, these missions face numerous challenges, including lack of resources, support, and clear mandate. It is important for the UN to address these challenges and continue to improve its peacekeeping operations to effectively maintain peace and stability around the world.





### Subsection: 9.2a NATO and Intervention

The North Atlantic Treaty Organization (NATO) is one of the most prominent regional organizations involved in military intervention. It is a military alliance between the United States and several European countries, with the primary goal of safeguarding the freedom and security of its member states. In this section, we will examine the role of NATO in intervention and its impact on international relations.

#### NATO's Role in Intervention

NATO has been involved in various interventions, both in Europe and beyond. One of the most notable interventions was the NATO intervention in Libya in 2011, which aimed to protect civilians from the oppressive regime of Muammar Gaddafi. The intervention was authorized by the United Nations Security Council and was led by NATO forces, primarily the United States, France, and the United Kingdom.

The intervention was successful in achieving its goal of protecting civilians, but it also faced criticism for its prolonged duration and the loss of civilian lives. The intervention also had a significant impact on the region, leading to the downfall of Gaddafi's regime and the subsequent civil war in Libya.

#### NATO's Impact on International Relations

NATO's interventions have had a significant impact on international relations, particularly in the Middle East. The intervention in Libya, for example, was seen as a violation of Libya's sovereignty by some countries, leading to strained relations between NATO and these countries.

Furthermore, NATO's intervention in Libya also raised concerns about the organization's role in international affairs. Some critics argue that NATO's intervention was motivated by its own interests, rather than solely protecting civilians. This has led to debates about the legitimacy and effectiveness of NATO's interventions.

#### Conclusion

In conclusion, NATO plays a crucial role in intervention, particularly in Europe and the Middle East. Its interventions have had a significant impact on international relations, both positive and negative. As NATO continues to evolve and adapt to new challenges, its role in intervention will continue to be a topic of discussion and debate.





### Subsection: 9.2b African Union and Intervention

The African Union (AU) is a continental organization consisting of 55 member states in Africa. It was established in 2002 with the goal of promoting unity, peace, and development in Africa. The AU has been involved in various interventions in Africa, with a focus on promoting peace and stability.

#### AU's Role in Intervention

The AU has been involved in interventions in various African countries, including Sudan, Somalia, and Libya. One of the most notable interventions was the AU's involvement in the conflict in Darfur, Sudan. The AU deployed a peacekeeping mission, known as the African Union Mission in Sudan (AMIS), to the region in 2004. The mission aimed to protect civilians and facilitate humanitarian aid.

The AU's intervention in Darfur faced challenges, including limited resources and security concerns. However, it played a crucial role in providing humanitarian aid and protecting civilians in the region. The AU's intervention also paved the way for a larger UN peacekeeping mission, known as the United Nations-African Union Mission in Darfur (UNAMID), which was deployed in 2007.

#### AU's Impact on International Relations

The AU's interventions have had a significant impact on international relations, particularly in Africa. The organization's involvement in conflicts has been seen as a positive step towards promoting peace and stability in the region. It has also been seen as a way for African countries to take ownership of their own conflicts and find solutions that are tailored to their specific needs.

However, the AU's interventions have also faced criticism. Some argue that the organization's limited resources and lack of military capabilities make its interventions ineffective. Others argue that the AU's interventions are often driven by political agendas and do not always prioritize the needs of the affected populations.

Despite these challenges, the AU's role in intervention has been crucial in promoting peace and stability in Africa. As the organization continues to grow and develop, its role in intervention is likely to become even more significant.





### Subsection: 9.2c ASEAN and Intervention

The Association of Southeast Asian Nations (ASEAN) is a regional organization consisting of ten member states in Southeast Asia. It was established in 1967 with the goal of promoting economic growth, social progress, and cultural development in the region. The ASEAN has been involved in various interventions in the region, with a focus on promoting peace and stability.

#### ASEAN's Role in Intervention

The ASEAN has been involved in interventions in various Southeast Asian countries, including Indonesia, Malaysia, and the Philippines. One of the most notable interventions was the ASEAN's involvement in the conflict in Mindanao, Philippines. The ASEAN deployed a peacekeeping mission, known as the ASEAN Regional Forum (ARF), to the region in 1994. The mission aimed to address the root causes of the conflict and promote reconciliation between the conflicting parties.

The ASEAN's intervention in Mindanao faced challenges, including limited resources and security concerns. However, it played a crucial role in providing humanitarian aid and promoting reconciliation in the region. The ASEAN's intervention also paved the way for a larger UN peacekeeping mission, known as the United Nations Mission in the Philippines (UNMIP), which was deployed in 2000.

#### ASEAN's Impact on International Relations

The ASEAN's interventions have had a significant impact on international relations, particularly in Southeast Asia. The organization's involvement in conflicts has been seen as a positive step towards promoting peace and stability in the region. It has also been seen as a way for Southeast Asian countries to take ownership of their own conflicts and find solutions that are tailored to their specific needs.

However, the ASEAN's interventions have also faced criticism. Some argue that the organization's limited resources and lack of military capabilities make its interventions ineffective. Others argue that the ASEAN's interventions are often driven by political agendas and do not always prioritize the needs of the affected populations.

Despite these challenges, the ASEAN's role in intervention has been crucial in promoting peace and stability in Southeast Asia. Its interventions have also served as a model for other regional organizations, demonstrating the importance of regional cooperation in addressing conflicts and promoting peace. 


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the role of international organizations in great power military intervention. We have seen how these organizations play a crucial role in shaping the dynamics of intervention and how they can either facilitate or hinder the effectiveness of such interventions. We have also discussed the various challenges and limitations faced by these organizations in their efforts to regulate and oversee great power military intervention.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of international cooperation and coordination in addressing global security issues. International organizations provide a platform for countries to come together and work towards common goals, making them essential players in the realm of military intervention. However, we have also seen how the lack of consensus and conflicting interests among member states can hinder the effectiveness of these organizations.

Furthermore, we have examined the role of international law and norms in regulating great power military intervention. These legal frameworks and norms serve as guidelines for states to follow and help prevent abuses of power. However, we have also seen how these norms can be manipulated and violated by powerful states, highlighting the need for stronger enforcement mechanisms.

In conclusion, international organizations play a crucial role in great power military intervention, but their effectiveness is limited by various factors such as conflicting interests, lack of consensus, and weak enforcement mechanisms. It is essential for these organizations to continue to work towards improving their effectiveness and promoting international cooperation in addressing global security issues.

# Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

## Chapter 10: The Effectiveness of Great Power Military Intervention




### Introduction

In the realm of international relations, the role of non-state actors has become increasingly significant. These actors, which include non-governmental organizations (NGOs), multinational corporations, and religious groups, often have their own agendas and interests that may align or conflict with those of great powers. In this chapter, we will delve into the complex and multifaceted role of non-state actors in great power military intervention.

Non-state actors have been instrumental in shaping the dynamics of international conflicts, particularly in the context of great power interventions. Their involvement can range from providing humanitarian aid and diplomatic support to engaging in combat operations. Their actions can significantly influence the outcome of interventions, and understanding their role is crucial for a comprehensive study of great power military intervention.

This chapter will explore the various ways in which non-state actors interact with great powers in the context of military intervention. We will examine their motivations, strategies, and the impact of their involvement on the outcome of interventions. We will also discuss the challenges and opportunities that non-state actors present for great powers, and how these actors can be effectively engaged in interventions.

The role of non-state actors in great power military intervention is a complex and multifaceted topic that requires a comprehensive understanding of international relations, conflict dynamics, and the motivations and strategies of these actors. This chapter aims to provide a thorough analysis of this topic, shedding light on the intricate dynamics of great power interventions and the role of non-state actors therein. 




### Subsection: 10.1a Humanitarian NGOs

Non-governmental organizations (NGOs) play a crucial role in great power military intervention, particularly in the context of humanitarian crises. These organizations, which are often funded by governments or private donors, provide aid and assistance to populations affected by conflict or natural disasters. In this section, we will focus on one type of NGO - humanitarian NGOs - and their role in great power military intervention.

#### The Role of Humanitarian NGOs in Great Power Military Intervention

Humanitarian NGOs are non-profit organizations that provide aid and assistance to populations affected by conflict or natural disasters. They operate in areas where the government is unable or unwilling to provide adequate assistance. Humanitarian NGOs are often the first responders in a crisis, providing immediate relief and support to affected populations.

In the context of great power military intervention, humanitarian NGOs play a critical role. They provide much-needed aid and assistance to populations affected by the intervention, often operating in areas that are not accessible to government forces. Their presence can help alleviate the humanitarian crisis and improve the overall situation on the ground.

However, the involvement of humanitarian NGOs in great power military intervention is not without challenges. The presence of these organizations can be seen as a threat by both the intervening power and the target country. The intervening power may view the NGOs as potential competitors for influence and control, while the target country may see them as a threat to its sovereignty.

#### The Humanitarian Cluster System

To address these challenges, the United Nations has established the Humanitarian Cluster System. This system aims to improve the coordination and effectiveness of humanitarian NGOs in disaster-affected countries. The system is based on the concept of "clusters," which are groups of organizations responsible for specific sectors, such as health, nutrition, and water and sanitation.

The Humanitarian Cluster System has been criticized for its reliance on international humanitarian agencies and exclusion of local and national organizations from coordination activities. However, it has also been praised for its ability to improve coordination and avoid duplication of efforts.

#### The Code of Conduct for the International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement and Non-Governmental Organizations

In addition to the Humanitarian Cluster System, humanitarian NGOs are also bound by the Code of Conduct for the International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement and Non-Governmental Organizations. This code outlines the principles and values that guide the actions of humanitarian NGOs, including impartiality, independence, and accountability.

The Code of Conduct also emphasizes the importance of coordination and cooperation among humanitarian NGOs. It states that "coordination is essential to ensure that the assistance provided by different organizations does not result in duplication of efforts or in the neglect of certain sectors or regions." This coordination is crucial in the context of great power military intervention, where the presence of multiple NGOs can lead to confusion and inefficiency if not properly coordinated.

In conclusion, humanitarian NGOs play a vital role in great power military intervention. Their presence can help alleviate the humanitarian crisis and improve the overall situation on the ground. However, their involvement also presents challenges that must be addressed through effective coordination and cooperation. The Humanitarian Cluster System and the Code of Conduct for the International Red Cross and Red Crescent Movement and Non-Governmental Organizations provide frameworks for addressing these challenges and improving the effectiveness of humanitarian NGOs in great power military intervention.





### Subsection: 10.1b Advocacy NGOs

Advocacy non-governmental organizations (NGOs) play a crucial role in great power military intervention, particularly in the context of humanitarian crises. These organizations, which are often funded by governments or private donors, advocate for the rights and needs of specific groups or causes. In this section, we will focus on one type of advocacy NGO - human rights NGOs - and their role in great power military intervention.

#### The Role of Human Rights NGOs in Great Power Military Intervention

Human rights NGOs are non-profit organizations that advocate for the protection and promotion of human rights. They operate in areas where human rights are being violated, often in the context of great power military intervention. Human rights NGOs play a critical role in documenting human rights violations, advocating for justice and accountability, and providing support to affected communities.

In the context of great power military intervention, human rights NGOs play a crucial role. They provide a voice for affected populations, often documenting human rights violations that may go unnoticed by the intervening power. Their work can help shed light on the humanitarian crisis and inform the intervention strategy.

However, the involvement of human rights NGOs in great power military intervention is not without challenges. The presence of these organizations can be seen as a threat by both the intervening power and the target country. The intervening power may view the NGOs as potential competitors for influence and control, while the target country may see them as a threat to its sovereignty.

#### The Role of Advocacy NGOs in Great Power Military Intervention

Advocacy NGOs, in general, play a crucial role in great power military intervention. These organizations advocate for specific causes or groups, often working to influence policy and decision-making processes. In the context of military intervention, advocacy NGOs can play a critical role in shaping the intervention strategy and ensuring that the needs and rights of affected populations are considered.

For example, in the context of the Syrian Civil War, advocacy NGOs have been instrumental in advocating for the protection of civilians and the provision of humanitarian aid. Their work has helped bring attention to the ongoing humanitarian crisis and has influenced the intervention strategies of various great powers involved in the conflict.

However, the involvement of advocacy NGOs in great power military intervention is not without challenges. The presence of these organizations can be seen as a threat by both the intervening power and the target country. The intervening power may view the NGOs as potential competitors for influence and control, while the target country may see them as a threat to its sovereignty.

#### The Role of Advocacy NGOs in Great Power Military Intervention

Advocacy NGOs, in general, play a crucial role in great power military intervention. These organizations advocate for specific causes or groups, often working to influence policy and decision-making processes. In the context of military intervention, advocacy NGOs can play a critical role in shaping the intervention strategy and ensuring that the needs and rights of affected populations are considered.

For example, in the context of the Syrian Civil War, advocacy NGOs have been instrumental in advocating for the protection of civilians and the provision of humanitarian aid. However, the involvement of advocacy NGOs in great power military intervention is not without challenges. The presence of these organizations can be seen as a threat by both the intervening power and the target country. The intervening power may view the NGOs as potential competitors for influence and control, while the target country may see them as a threat to its sovereignty.




### Subsection: 10.1c Challenges and Critiques

The involvement of non-state actors, particularly non-governmental organizations (NGOs), in great power military intervention is not without its challenges and criticisms. While these organizations play a crucial role in documenting human rights violations and advocating for justice and accountability, their involvement can also lead to a number of challenges and criticisms.

#### Challenges Faced by NGOs in Great Power Military Intervention

One of the main challenges faced by NGOs in great power military intervention is the issue of access. Many NGOs operate in areas that are not easily accessible due to ongoing conflict or instability. This can make it difficult for these organizations to carry out their work effectively. For example, in the case of the Syrian Civil War, many NGOs have faced challenges in accessing areas affected by the conflict due to ongoing violence and instability.

Another challenge faced by NGOs is the issue of safety. Working in areas of conflict can be dangerous, and NGO workers are often at risk of violence and harm. This can make it difficult for these organizations to carry out their work, particularly in areas where there is a high level of violence and instability.

#### Criticisms of NGOs in Great Power Military Intervention

Despite their crucial role in great power military intervention, NGOs have also faced criticism. One of the main criticisms is the issue of bias. Some critics argue that NGOs may have a bias towards certain groups or causes, which can influence their reporting and advocacy efforts. This can lead to a lack of objectivity and can undermine their credibility.

Another criticism is the issue of accountability. Some critics argue that NGOs are not held accountable for their actions and decisions, particularly in the context of great power military intervention. This can lead to a lack of transparency and can raise questions about the effectiveness and impact of their work.

#### Conclusion

Despite these challenges and criticisms, NGOs continue to play a crucial role in great power military intervention. Their work is essential in documenting human rights violations and advocating for justice and accountability. However, it is important to address these challenges and criticisms in order to ensure the effectiveness and credibility of NGOs in these contexts.




### Subsection: 10.2a Definition and Role

Private military companies (PMCs) are private companies that provide military and security services to governments, international organizations, and other non-state actors. These companies are often hired by governments to provide services such as training, logistics, and security support in conflict zones. They are also hired by international organizations, such as the United Nations, to provide security and logistical support in peacekeeping missions.

The role of PMCs in great power military intervention is complex and multifaceted. On one hand, they are seen as a cost-effective and efficient alternative to traditional military deployment. By outsourcing certain military and security functions, governments can save resources and reduce the risk to their own soldiers. PMCs also bring specialized skills and expertise that may not be available within a government's own military.

On the other hand, the use of PMCs has also raised ethical and legal concerns. The use of private companies in military operations blurs the lines between combatants and civilians, and raises questions about accountability and liability. PMCs are not subject to the same rules of engagement and oversight as traditional military forces, and this can lead to abuses and human rights violations.

The role of PMCs in great power military intervention is also influenced by the concept of "asymmetric warfare". Asymmetric warfare refers to the use of unconventional tactics and strategies by non-state actors to achieve their objectives. PMCs, with their specialized skills and expertise, are often hired to counter these tactics and provide a more conventional military response.

In addition to their role in great power military intervention, PMCs also play a significant role in the training and equipping of local forces in conflict zones. This is particularly evident in the case of the Syrian Civil War, where PMCs have been hired by various parties to train and equip local forces. This role raises questions about the effectiveness and sustainability of these efforts, as well as the potential for these local forces to be used for future interventions.

Overall, the role of PMCs in great power military intervention is complex and multifaceted. While they offer certain advantages, their use also raises ethical and legal concerns that must be carefully considered. As the use of PMCs continues to grow, it is important to carefully examine their role and impact in order to ensure responsible and ethical military intervention.





### Subsection: 10.2b Ethical and Legal Issues

The use of private military companies (PMCs) in great power military intervention raises a number of ethical and legal issues that must be addressed. These issues are not only important for the United States, but also for other great powers such as Russia and China, who also employ PMCs in their military operations.

#### Ethical Issues

The ethical issues surrounding the use of PMCs are complex and multifaceted. On one hand, the use of PMCs can be seen as a violation of the principle of just war, which states that only legitimate authorities can declare war and use force. By outsourcing military operations to private companies, great powers may be circumventing this principle and engaging in unjust war.

Furthermore, the use of PMCs also raises concerns about the protection of human rights. PMCs are not subject to the same rules of engagement and oversight as traditional military forces, which can lead to abuses and human rights violations. This is particularly concerning in conflict zones where civilians are already at risk.

On the other hand, the use of PMCs can also be seen as a necessary evil in the face of complex and unconventional threats. PMCs bring specialized skills and expertise that may not be available within a government's own military, and their use can save resources and reduce the risk to soldiers. This argument aligns with the principle of proportionality, which states that the use of force must be proportional to the threat.

#### Legal Issues

The legal issues surrounding the use of PMCs are also complex and multifaceted. The use of PMCs raises questions about accountability and liability. PMCs are not subject to the same legal framework as traditional military forces, and this can make it difficult to hold them accountable for their actions. This is particularly concerning in cases where PMCs are hired by multiple parties, each with their own interests and objectives.

Furthermore, the use of PMCs also raises questions about the legality of their operations. In some cases, PMCs may be operating in areas where they are not authorized to do so, or they may be engaging in activities that are prohibited by international law. This can lead to legal challenges and potential legal consequences for both the PMCs and the great powers employing them.

#### Conclusion

The ethical and legal issues surrounding the use of PMCs in great power military intervention are complex and multifaceted. While the use of PMCs can bring benefits such as specialized skills and expertise, it also raises concerns about the protection of human rights and the legality of their operations. As the use of PMCs continues to grow, it is important for great powers to address these issues and establish clear guidelines and regulations to ensure the ethical and legal use of PMCs in military operations.





### Subsection: 10.2c Case Studies

To further understand the role of private military companies (PMCs) in great power military intervention, it is important to examine case studies of their use in different conflicts. By analyzing these case studies, we can gain a better understanding of the ethical and legal issues surrounding the use of PMCs and their impact on the outcome of interventions.

#### Case Study 1: Blackwater in Iraq

One of the most well-known and controversial case studies of PMCs is the use of the private security company Blackwater in Iraq. Blackwater was hired by the United States government to provide security services in Iraq, particularly in the dangerous city of Fallujah. In 2007, Blackwater employees were involved in a shooting incident in which 17 civilians were killed. This incident sparked international outrage and raised questions about the accountability and oversight of PMCs.

The use of Blackwater in Iraq also raises ethical concerns about the protection of human rights. The company's actions in Fallujah were seen as a violation of the principle of proportionality, as their use of force was deemed excessive and disproportionate to the threat. This case also highlights the legal issues surrounding the use of PMCs, as Blackwater employees were not held accountable for their actions due to the lack of a clear legal framework for PMCs.

#### Case Study 2: Academi in Afghanistan

Another case study of PMCs is the use of the company Academi (formerly known as Blackwater) in Afghanistan. Academi was hired by the United States government to provide training services to the Afghan National Army. However, in 2010, it was revealed that Academi employees had engaged in unauthorized and excessive use of force while training Afghan soldiers.

This case raises ethical concerns about the protection of human rights, as the actions of Academi employees were seen as a violation of the principle of proportionality. It also highlights the legal issues surrounding the use of PMCs, as Academi employees were not held accountable for their actions due to the lack of a clear legal framework for PMCs.

#### Case Study 3: G4S in the UK

A less well-known but equally important case study is the use of the private security company G4S in the UK. G4S was hired by the UK government to provide security services at the London Olympics in 2012. However, it was revealed that G4S had failed to properly train and vet their employees, leading to security breaches and concerns about the safety of athletes and visitors.

This case raises ethical concerns about the protection of human rights, as the actions of G4S employees were seen as a violation of the principle of proportionality. It also highlights the legal issues surrounding the use of PMCs, as G4S was not held accountable for their actions due to the lack of a clear legal framework for PMCs.

### Conclusion

These case studies demonstrate the complex and multifaceted nature of the role of PMCs in great power military intervention. They highlight the ethical and legal issues surrounding the use of PMCs and the need for a clear legal framework to regulate their actions. As great powers continue to rely on PMCs in their military operations, it is crucial to address these issues and ensure the protection of human rights and the accountability of PMCs.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the role of non-state actors in great power military intervention. We have seen how these actors, such as private military companies and non-governmental organizations, play a significant role in shaping the outcome of interventions. We have also discussed the challenges and opportunities that come with their involvement, and the ethical considerations that must be taken into account.

One of the key takeaways from this chapter is the importance of understanding the motivations and interests of non-state actors in any intervention. Their actions and decisions can have a significant impact on the success or failure of a military intervention, and it is crucial for policymakers and military leaders to consider their role in the planning and execution of interventions.

Furthermore, we have also highlighted the need for transparency and accountability in the use of non-state actors in military interventions. The lack of regulations and oversight can lead to abuses and violations of human rights, which can have long-lasting consequences. It is essential for great powers to establish clear guidelines and regulations for the use of non-state actors in interventions, and to hold them accountable for their actions.

In conclusion, the role of non-state actors in great power military intervention is complex and multifaceted. Their involvement can bring both challenges and opportunities, and it is crucial for policymakers and military leaders to carefully consider their role in interventions. By understanding their motivations and establishing clear guidelines and regulations, we can ensure that interventions are carried out in a responsible and ethical manner.
