# Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

## Chapter 14: Intervention and Its Impact




### Section: 13.1c Global Power Shifts

As we continue to look towards the future, it is important to consider the ongoing global power shifts that are occurring. These shifts are not only impacting the traditional great powers, but also the emerging powers such as Turkey, Poland, and Japan.

Turkey, with its strong military and economic influence, is expected to continue expanding its sphere of influence into the Arab world and Russia. This will likely lead to increased intervention in these regions, as Turkey competes with other powers for influence.

Japan, on the other hand, is expected to become a major power in the Pacific region. With its growing military strength and economic influence, Japan will be able to project power across East Asia. This will likely lead to increased intervention in the region, as Japan competes with other powers for influence.

Poland, with its strong military alliance and economic influence, is also expected to become a major power. With its expanding influence into what was formerly European Russia, Poland will likely be involved in interventions in this region.

These global power shifts will have a significant impact on intervention in the future. As new powers emerge and traditional powers decline, the dynamics of intervention will continue to evolve. It is important for policymakers and scholars to closely monitor these shifts and their potential implications for intervention.





### Section: 13.2 Debates and Controversies:

#### 13.2a Intervention vs. Non-Intervention

The debate over intervention versus non-intervention has been a long-standing one in the field of international relations. Intervention refers to the involvement of one state in the affairs of another state, while non-intervention refers to the principle of non-interference in the internal affairs of other states. This debate has been particularly relevant in the context of great power military intervention, as these interventions often involve the use of force and have significant implications for both the intervening state and the state being intervened in.

One of the key arguments in favor of intervention is the responsibility to protect (R2P). This principle, which was first introduced in 2005, allows for intervention in cases where there is a responsibility to protect civilians from mass atrocities. This principle has been used to justify interventions in Libya, Syria, and other countries where there have been reports of human rights violations. However, the implementation of R2P has been controversial, with some arguing that it has been used selectively and has led to unintended consequences.

On the other hand, proponents of non-intervention argue that intervention can lead to a violation of sovereignty and can have unintended consequences. They also argue that intervention can be used as a tool for imperialism and neo-colonialism, as seen in the historical context of European colonization and intervention in Africa. Additionally, non-interventionists argue that intervention can lead to a power imbalance, as the intervening state may have a stronger military and economic power, giving them an unfair advantage in the intervention.

The debate over intervention versus non-intervention is complex and multifaceted. It is important for policymakers and scholars to consider the potential implications and consequences of both intervention and non-intervention in order to make informed decisions. As we continue to see great power military interventions in the future, it is crucial to have a nuanced understanding of this debate and its implications for global politics.





### Subsection: 13.2b Human Rights vs. National Interests

The debate over human rights versus national interests is a crucial aspect of great power military intervention. This debate is often framed as a conflict between the responsibility of a state to protect its own citizens and the responsibility of a state to uphold international human rights laws.

On one hand, proponents of human rights argue that a state's responsibility to protect its own citizens should not take precedence over its responsibility to uphold international human rights laws. They argue that a state's actions, such as military intervention, should be guided by the principles of human rights and should not be used as a tool to further its own national interests. This perspective is often supported by the principle of R2P, which emphasizes the responsibility of states to protect civilians from mass atrocities.

On the other hand, proponents of national interests argue that a state's responsibility to protect its own citizens should take precedence over its responsibility to uphold international human rights laws. They argue that a state's actions, such as military intervention, should be guided by its own national interests and should not be constrained by international laws and norms. This perspective is often supported by the concept of sovereignty, which emphasizes a state's right to govern itself without interference from external powers.

The debate over human rights versus national interests is complex and multifaceted. It is important for policymakers and scholars to consider the potential implications and consequences of both perspectives in order to make informed decisions about military intervention.

### Subsection: 13.2c Future of Intervention

As we look towards the future, it is important to consider the potential impact of great power military intervention on global politics. The future of intervention will be shaped by a variety of factors, including technological advancements, changes in international law and norms, and shifts in global power dynamics.

One potential future scenario is the increased use of technology in military intervention. With advancements in technology, such as artificial intelligence and autonomous weapons, the role of human soldiers in military intervention may become obsolete. This could lead to a shift in the way great powers intervene in conflicts, with a greater emphasis on technology and less on traditional military tactics.

Another potential future scenario is the evolution of international law and norms surrounding military intervention. As global power dynamics continue to shift, there may be a reevaluation of existing laws and norms related to intervention. This could lead to a more permissive or restrictive approach to intervention, depending on the perspectives of the dominant global powers.

Finally, the future of intervention will also be shaped by changes in global power dynamics. As new powers emerge and existing powers decline, the dynamics of intervention may also change. This could lead to a shift in the types of conflicts that are intervened in, as well as the methods and motivations behind intervention.

In conclusion, the future of intervention is uncertain and will be shaped by a variety of factors. It is important for policymakers and scholars to continue studying and analyzing intervention in order to better understand its potential impact on global politics. By examining the past and present of intervention, we can gain valuable insights into the future and work towards a more peaceful and just world.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have explored the future of intervention by great powers. We have discussed the potential challenges and opportunities that lie ahead, as well as the potential impact of intervention on both the intervening country and the target country. We have also examined the role of international law and organizations in regulating intervention, and the importance of considering human rights and ethical considerations in intervention decisions.

As we have seen, intervention is a complex and multifaceted issue that requires careful consideration and planning. It is not a one-size-fits-all solution, and each intervention must be approached with a unique set of factors in mind. However, by understanding the history and current state of intervention, as well as the potential future developments, we can better prepare for and navigate these complex situations.

In conclusion, intervention will continue to be a crucial aspect of international relations, and it is important for policymakers and scholars to continue studying and analyzing it. By doing so, we can gain a deeper understanding of its potential benefits and drawbacks, and work towards more effective and ethical interventions in the future.

## Chapter 14: Intervention Effectiveness and Legitimacy




### Subsection: 13.2c Unilateral vs. Multilateral Intervention

The future of intervention will also be shaped by the ongoing debate over unilateral versus multilateral intervention. Unilateral intervention refers to the use of military force by a single state without the consent or support of other states. Multilateral intervention, on the other hand, involves the use of military force by multiple states with the consent and support of all parties involved.

Proponents of unilateral intervention argue that it allows for quicker and more decisive action, as there is no need to negotiate or coordinate with other states. They also argue that it allows for a state to protect its own national interests without being hindered by the interests of other states. However, critics of unilateral intervention argue that it can lead to a lack of legitimacy and support from the international community, as well as potential backlash and retaliation from other states.

Proponents of multilateral intervention argue that it allows for a more comprehensive and coordinated approach to intervention, with the involvement of multiple states and perspectives. They also argue that it can provide a stronger basis for legitimacy and support from the international community. However, critics of multilateral intervention argue that it can be slow and cumbersome, as well as difficult to coordinate and enforce among multiple states.

As we look towards the future, it is important to consider the potential implications and consequences of both unilateral and multilateral intervention. The future of intervention will also be shaped by advancements in technology, such as the development of autonomous weapons and artificial intelligence, which could potentially impact the effectiveness and ethics of intervention. Additionally, the changing global power dynamics and the rise of new powers, such as China and India, will also play a role in shaping the future of intervention.

In conclusion, the future of intervention is complex and uncertain, but it is important for policymakers and scholars to continue studying and debating the various aspects of intervention in order to make informed decisions and shape the future of intervention in a responsible and ethical manner.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the future of intervention by great powers. We have discussed the potential challenges and opportunities that lie ahead, as well as the potential impact of intervention on both the intervening state and the state being intervened in. We have also examined the role of international law and organizations in regulating and guiding intervention efforts.

As we have seen, intervention is a complex and multifaceted issue that requires careful consideration and planning. It is not a one-size-fits-all solution and must be approached with caution and sensitivity. The future of intervention will continue to be shaped by a variety of factors, including technological advancements, changes in global power dynamics, and evolving international norms and laws.

It is our hope that this comprehensive study has provided readers with a deeper understanding of intervention and its potential implications. We encourage further research and discussion on this topic, as it is crucial for policymakers and scholars to continue examining and evaluating intervention strategies in order to improve their effectiveness and minimize potential harm.

## Chapter: Chapter 14: Conclusion

We have also delved into the various forms of intervention, such as direct military intervention, economic sanctions, and diplomatic intervention.

One of the key themes that emerged from our study is the importance of understanding the underlying motivations and interests of great powers when it comes to intervention. We have seen how these motivations can range from protecting national security and promoting democracy to pursuing economic interests and expanding influence. It is crucial for policymakers and scholars to carefully consider these motivations when analyzing and evaluating intervention strategies.

Another important aspect of our study is the recognition of the potential consequences and unintended effects of intervention. We have seen how intervention can have both positive and negative outcomes, and how these outcomes can be difficult to predict and control. It is essential for policymakers to carefully consider the potential consequences of intervention and to have a clear understanding of the potential risks and unintended effects.

However, it is clear that intervention will continue to play a significant role in international affairs. The rise of new powers and the changing nature of conflicts will require great powers to adapt and evolve their intervention strategies.

One of the key challenges for intervention in the future will be the increasing complexity of conflicts. With the rise of non-state actors and cyber warfare, traditional military interventions may not be as effective. Great powers will need to develop new strategies and technologies to address these challenges.

On the other hand, there are also opportunities for intervention to become more targeted and effective. With advancements in technology and data analysis, great powers can gather more information and make more informed decisions about when and how to intervene.

In conclusion, the future of intervention is uncertain, but it is clear that great powers will continue to play a crucial role in global conflicts. As we move forward, it is essential to carefully consider the potential consequences and implications of intervention, and to strive for more effective and ethical approaches.

# Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

## Chapter 14: Future of Intervention




### Introduction

The Syrian Civil War, which began in 2011, has been a complex and devastating conflict that has involved multiple actors and interventions. The intervention in Syria by great powers has been a topic of great interest and debate among scholars and policymakers. In this chapter, we will delve into a comprehensive study of the intervention in Syria by great powers, examining the various factors that influenced their decisions to intervene and the consequences of their actions.

The intervention in Syria has been a highly controversial topic, with different perspectives and opinions being expressed by various stakeholders. Some argue that the intervention was necessary to protect human rights and prevent further atrocities, while others argue that it was a violation of sovereignty and led to further instability and violence. This chapter aims to provide a balanced and objective analysis of the intervention, taking into account all perspectives and evidence.

We will begin by providing a brief overview of the Syrian Civil War and the key players involved. This will include a discussion of the historical and political context that led to the outbreak of the war and the various actors who have been involved in the conflict. We will then delve into the specific interventions by great powers, including the United States, Russia, and Turkey, and the reasons behind their decisions to intervene.

Next, we will examine the consequences of these interventions, both in terms of the conflict itself and the broader regional and global implications. This will include a discussion of the humanitarian crisis, the spread of extremism, and the impact on neighboring countries and international relations.

Finally, we will conclude with a critical analysis of the intervention in Syria, discussing the lessons learned and the implications for future interventions by great powers. This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive and objective analysis of the intervention in Syria, shedding light on the complex dynamics and consequences of great power military intervention.




### Subsection: 14.1a Historical Context

The intervention in Syria by great powers is a complex and multifaceted issue that requires a thorough understanding of the historical context. The roots of the conflict can be traced back to the early 20th century, when the Ottoman Empire, which had controlled the region for centuries, began to decline. This led to a power vacuum that was filled by various European powers, including France, Britain, and Russia.

The Syrian region was particularly important to these powers due to its strategic location and natural resources. France, in particular, had a strong interest in the region and established a mandate over Syria in 1920. However, this led to tensions with the local population, who saw the French as foreign occupiers. In response, the Syrian National Movement was formed, which aimed to achieve independence from French rule.

The French responded with repression, leading to a series of uprisings and rebellions. This ultimately led to the Syrian independence in 1946, but the country faced ongoing political instability and coups. In 1970, Hafez al-Assad seized power in a coup and established a dictatorship that lasted until his death in 2000. His son, Bashar al-Assad, succeeded him and continued the authoritarian rule.

Under the Assad regime, Syria became increasingly isolated from the international community due to its support for terrorist organizations and human rights abuses. This led to international efforts to intervene and address the ongoing humanitarian crisis in the country. However, these efforts were met with resistance from Russia, which saw Syria as a key ally in the region.

The intervention in Syria by great powers, particularly the United States, Russia, and Turkey, has been a topic of great interest and debate. The US intervention was primarily focused on combating ISIS and supporting rebel groups, while Russia and Turkey supported the Assad regime. This intervention has had significant consequences for the region, including the ongoing civil war and the displacement of millions of people.

In the next section, we will delve into the specific interventions by these great powers and the reasons behind their decisions to intervene. We will also examine the consequences of these interventions and the lessons learned for future interventions by great powers.




### Section: 14.1b The Syrian Civil War

The Syrian Civil War, which began in 2011, has been a complex and ongoing conflict that has involved various factions and external powers. The war has been marked by violence, human rights abuses, and a devastating humanitarian crisis.

The conflict began in March 2011, when political protests turned violent in response to the Syrian government's response to the Arab Spring. The protests were sparked by the arrest and torture of a group of teenagers who had painted anti-government graffiti on a wall in the city of Daraa. This event, known as the Daraa uprising, led to widespread protests and demonstrations across the country, calling for political reform and an end to the Assad regime.

The Syrian government's response to the protests was brutal, with security forces using violence and torture to suppress the demonstrations. This led to the formation of armed opposition groups, who took up arms to fight against the government. The conflict quickly escalated, with the government using its superior military and financial resources to gain the upper hand.

The Syrian Civil War has been marked by numerous human rights abuses, including the use of chemical weapons by the Syrian government and its allies. In April 2014, Bellingcat, a non-profit organization that uses open source and social media investigation, published evidence of chemical weapons being used on Syrian civilians, including children. This evidence was collected and analyzed from video footage and images posted on social media platforms.

The use of chemical weapons in the Syrian Civil War has been a major concern for the international community. In response to the evidence presented by Bellingcat, the United Nations Security Council passed Resolution 2118, which called for the destruction of Syria's chemical weapons stockpile. However, the resolution was not fully implemented, and there have been numerous reports of chemical weapons being used by the Syrian government and its allies since then.

The Syrian Civil War has also been marked by the involvement of external powers. The United States, Russia, and Turkey have all been involved in the conflict, with the US and Turkey supporting rebel groups and Russia supporting the Assad regime. This intervention has had significant consequences for the conflict, with the involvement of these powers complicating the situation and prolonging the war.

In conclusion, the Syrian Civil War has been a complex and ongoing conflict that has had a profound impact on the country and its people. The involvement of external powers and the use of chemical weapons have added further layers of complexity to the conflict, making it a crucial case study for understanding great power military intervention. 




### Section: 14.1c International Response

The international response to the Syrian Civil War has been complex and multifaceted. The conflict has been a major focus of international attention, with various countries and organizations providing aid and support to the Syrian people. However, the response has also been marked by controversy and criticism, particularly in regards to the use of military intervention.

#### International Aid and Support

In response to the humanitarian crisis caused by the Syrian Civil War, the international community has provided significant aid and support to the Syrian people. This includes food, shelter, and medical assistance, as well as support for refugees who have fled the country. The United Nations and various non-governmental organizations (NGOs) have been instrumental in providing this aid.

The United Nations has been particularly active in its response to the Syrian Civil War. In 2014, the UN launched the Syria Crisis Response Plan, which aimed to provide aid to over 8 million people affected by the conflict. This plan was updated in 2015 to address the ongoing needs of the Syrian people. The UN has also been working to address the root causes of the conflict, including political instability and economic inequality.

#### Military Intervention

The use of military intervention in the Syrian Civil War has been a contentious issue. The Syrian government, with the support of its allies, has used military force to suppress the rebellion. This has resulted in significant civilian casualties and the destruction of infrastructure. In response, some countries have provided military support to the rebel groups, with the goal of overthrowing the Assad regime.

The United States, for example, has been providing military aid to the Syrian rebels since 2014. This aid includes training and equipment, as well as airstrikes targeting ISIS and other terrorist groups. However, there have been concerns about the effectiveness and potential unintended consequences of this intervention.

#### International Law and Human Rights

The Syrian Civil War has also raised important questions about international law and human rights. The use of chemical weapons by the Syrian government and its allies, as well as reports of human rights abuses by all parties involved, have been major concerns for the international community.

In response to these concerns, the United Nations has been working to hold those responsible for these violations accountable. The UN has established several commissions of inquiry to investigate human rights abuses in Syria, and has also referred the situation in Syria to the International Criminal Court.

#### Conclusion

The international response to the Syrian Civil War has been complex and multifaceted. While the international community has provided significant aid and support to the Syrian people, the use of military intervention has been a contentious issue. Moving forward, it will be important for the international community to continue providing aid and support, while also addressing the root causes of the conflict and holding those responsible for human rights abuses accountable.


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have examined the case study of intervention in Syria by great powers. We have seen how the intervention has been a complex and controversial issue, with various factors at play. From the initial protests in 2011 to the ongoing civil war, the intervention has had a significant impact on the region and its people.

We have also discussed the different approaches taken by the great powers involved, including the United States, Russia, and China. Each country has had its own interests and motivations for intervening in Syria, leading to varying levels of involvement and effectiveness.

Furthermore, we have explored the role of international organizations, such as the United Nations, in the intervention. The UN has played a crucial role in providing aid and support to the Syrian people, but its efforts have been hindered by the conflicting interests of the great powers.

Overall, the case study of intervention in Syria highlights the complexities and challenges of great power military intervention. It serves as a valuable lesson for future interventions and emphasizes the need for careful consideration and coordination among the involved parties.

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, conflicts and crises can arise in any corner of the world, affecting not just the affected country, but also the international community as a whole. In such situations, great powers, or major global powers, often have a significant role to play in addressing and resolving these conflicts. This chapter will delve into a case study of intervention by great powers, specifically focusing on the intervention in Yemen.

Yemen, a small country located in the Middle East, has been embroiled in a civil war since 2015, with various external powers involved in the conflict. The intervention in Yemen by great powers, including the United States, Saudi Arabia, and Iran, has been a complex and controversial issue, with far-reaching implications for the region and the world.

This chapter will provide a comprehensive study of the intervention in Yemen, examining the various factors that led to the intervention, the actions taken by the intervening powers, and the consequences of their involvement. It will also explore the role of international organizations and the impact of the intervention on the Yemeni people.

Through this case study, readers will gain a deeper understanding of the complexities and challenges of great power intervention, and the potential consequences of such actions. It will also serve as a valuable learning tool for those interested in international relations, conflict resolution, and humanitarian aid. So let us begin our exploration of the intervention in Yemen and the role of great powers in this conflict.


# Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

## Chapter 15: Case Study - Intervention in Yemen



### Section: 14.2 Analysis of Intervention:

The intervention in Syria has been a complex and multifaceted issue, with various actors and interests at play. In this section, we will analyze the actors and interests involved in the intervention, and how they have shaped the outcome of the conflict.

#### Actors and Interests

The intervention in Syria has involved a variety of actors, including the Syrian government, rebel groups, and foreign powers. Each of these actors has their own interests and motivations for their involvement in the conflict.

The Syrian government, led by President Bashar al-Assad, has been fighting to maintain control and suppress the rebellion. Their primary interest is to maintain their power and authority over the country. To achieve this, they have used military force to suppress the rebellion, resulting in significant civilian casualties and the destruction of infrastructure.

On the other hand, rebel groups in Syria have been fighting to overthrow the Assad regime and establish a new government. These groups have a diverse range of interests, including political, social, and religious motivations. Some rebel groups have received military support from foreign powers, such as the United States, Saudi Arabia, and Turkey, in an effort to overthrow the Assad regime.

Foreign powers have also played a significant role in the intervention in Syria. The United States, for example, has been providing military aid to the Syrian rebels since 2014. This aid includes training and equipment, as well as airstrikes targeting ISIS and other terrorist groups. However, there have been concerns about the effectiveness and potential unintended consequences of this intervention.

#### Interests and Outcomes

The interests of the various actors involved in the intervention have shaped the outcome of the conflict in Syria. The Syrian government's interest in maintaining control has led to the use of military force, resulting in a prolonged and devastating civil war. The rebel groups' interest in overthrowing the Assad regime has also contributed to the ongoing conflict, as they continue to fight for control of the country.

The involvement of foreign powers has also had a significant impact on the outcome of the conflict. While some foreign powers have provided military support to the rebels, others have been more cautious in their involvement. Russia, for example, has been a staunch supporter of the Syrian government and has provided military support to assist them in their fight against the rebels. This support has been crucial in maintaining the Assad regime's control over the country.

In conclusion, the intervention in Syria has been shaped by a complex web of actors and interests. The Syrian government, rebel groups, and foreign powers have all played a role in the ongoing conflict, with their interests and actions shaping the outcome of the intervention. As the conflict continues, it is essential to consider the interests and motivations of these actors in order to fully understand the complex dynamics of the intervention in Syria.




### Section: 14.2 Analysis of Intervention:

The intervention in Syria has been a complex and multifaceted issue, with various actors and interests at play. In this section, we will analyze the actors and interests involved in the intervention, and how they have shaped the outcome of the conflict.

#### Actors and Interests

The intervention in Syria has involved a variety of actors, including the Syrian government, rebel groups, and foreign powers. Each of these actors has their own interests and motivations for their involvement in the conflict.

The Syrian government, led by President Bashar al-Assad, has been fighting to maintain control and suppress the rebellion. Their primary interest is to maintain their power and authority over the country. To achieve this, they have used military force to suppress the rebellion, resulting in significant civilian casualties and the destruction of infrastructure.

On the other hand, rebel groups in Syria have been fighting to overthrow the Assad regime and establish a new government. These groups have a diverse range of interests, including political, social, and religious motivations. Some rebel groups have received military support from foreign powers, such as the United States, Saudi Arabia, and Turkey, in an effort to overthrow the Assad regime.

Foreign powers have also played a significant role in the intervention in Syria. The United States, for example, has been providing military aid to the Syrian rebels since 2014. This aid includes training and equipment, as well as airstrikes targeting ISIS and other terrorist groups. However, there have been concerns about the effectiveness and potential unintended consequences of this intervention.

#### Interests and Outcomes

The interests of the various actors involved in the intervention have shaped the outcome of the conflict in Syria. The Syrian government's interest in maintaining control has led to the use of military force, resulting in a prolonged and devastating civil war. The involvement of rebel groups and foreign powers has further complicated the situation, with each actor pursuing their own interests and agendas.

The intervention in Syria has also had significant implications for the region and the world. The ongoing conflict has resulted in a refugee crisis, with millions of Syrians fleeing their homes and seeking safety in neighboring countries and Europe. The intervention has also had economic impacts, with the Syrian economy suffering significant damage and the country facing economic sanctions from foreign powers.

In terms of the outcome of the intervention, the Syrian government has managed to maintain control over most of the country, but at a significant cost in terms of human lives and infrastructure. The rebel groups have been unable to overthrow the Assad regime, and the involvement of foreign powers has only further complicated the situation. The intervention in Syria serves as a cautionary tale about the potential consequences of military intervention and the importance of understanding the interests and motivations of all actors involved.





### Subsection: 14.2c Outcomes and Impacts

The intervention in Syria has had significant outcomes and impacts on the country and its people. These outcomes and impacts have been shaped by the interests and actions of the various actors involved in the conflict.

#### Outcomes

The intervention in Syria has resulted in a prolonged and devastating civil war, with no clear end in sight. The conflict has claimed hundreds of thousands of lives and has displaced millions of people, both within and outside of the country. The intervention has also led to the rise of terrorist groups, such as ISIS, which have carried out numerous attacks both in Syria and around the world.

The intervention has also had significant impacts on the country's infrastructure and economy. The ongoing conflict has resulted in the destruction of homes, schools, and other vital infrastructure, leaving many people without access to basic services. The economy has also been severely impacted, with many industries and businesses struggling to operate in the midst of the conflict.

#### Impacts

The intervention in Syria has also had significant impacts on the region and the world. The conflict has created a refugee crisis, with millions of people fleeing the country and seeking safety in neighboring countries and beyond. This has put a strain on the resources and economies of these countries, and has also led to increased tensions and conflicts.

The intervention has also had implications for international relations. The involvement of foreign powers in the conflict has led to increased tensions and conflicts between these powers, particularly between the United States and Russia. The intervention has also raised questions about the effectiveness and consequences of military intervention in conflicts, and has sparked debates about the use of force and the responsibility of great powers in global conflicts.

In conclusion, the intervention in Syria has had significant outcomes and impacts on the country and its people, as well as on the region and the world. The interests and actions of the various actors involved in the conflict have shaped these outcomes and impacts, and have raised important questions about the use of force and the responsibility of great powers in global conflicts. 


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have examined the case of intervention in Syria by great powers. We have seen how the intervention has had a significant impact on the country and its people, both positive and negative. We have also discussed the various factors that influenced the decision for intervention, including political, economic, and humanitarian concerns.

Through our analysis, we have found that intervention in Syria has been a complex and multifaceted issue. It has involved not only the actions of great powers, but also the involvement of regional and local actors. The intervention has also had far-reaching consequences, affecting not only Syria, but also the surrounding countries and the international community as a whole.

As we conclude this chapter, it is important to note that intervention in Syria is just one example of the many cases of intervention by great powers. Each case is unique and requires careful analysis and consideration. It is our hope that this comprehensive study has provided readers with a deeper understanding of the complexities and implications of intervention in Syria, and will serve as a valuable resource for further research and discussion on this topic.

Using the case of intervention in Syria as a starting point, research and analyze the factors that influenced the decision for intervention in another country. Consider political, economic, and humanitarian concerns, as well as the involvement of regional and local actors.

#### Exercise 2: Examining the Consequences of Intervention
Choose a specific aspect of intervention in Syria, such as the humanitarian crisis or the involvement of regional powers, and examine its consequences. Consider the short-term and long-term effects on the country and its people, as well as the impact on the international community.

#### Exercise 3: Comparing Intervention in Syria to Other Cases
Select another case of intervention by great powers and compare it to the intervention in Syria. Consider the similarities and differences in the factors influencing intervention, the actions taken, and the consequences.

#### Exercise 4: Discussing the Ethics of Intervention
Research and discuss the ethical considerations surrounding intervention in Syria. Consider the principles of just war theory and the responsibility of great powers to intervene in conflicts.

Based on your understanding of the case of intervention in Syria, propose a different approach that could have been taken by great powers. Consider the potential benefits and drawbacks of this approach and how it could have impacted the outcome of the intervention.


## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, military intervention by great powers has become a common occurrence. Whether it is in the form of direct military intervention or indirect support for rebel groups, great powers have been involved in conflicts around the world. One such example is the intervention in Yemen, which has been a topic of great interest and debate among scholars and policymakers. In this chapter, we will delve into a case study of intervention in Yemen, examining the various factors that led to the intervention and its consequences. We will also explore the different perspectives and approaches taken by various actors involved in the intervention, including the United States, Saudi Arabia, and Iran. By studying this case, we hope to gain a deeper understanding of the complexities and implications of great power military intervention.


# Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

## Chapter 15: Case Study - Intervention in Yemen




### Conclusion

The intervention in Syria by great powers has been a complex and controversial topic. The conflict has been ongoing since 2011 and has involved multiple actors, including the Syrian government, rebel groups, and foreign powers. The intervention by great powers, such as the United States, Russia, and Turkey, has had a significant impact on the conflict and the country as a whole.

One of the key findings of this case study is the importance of international law and norms in guiding great power intervention. The intervention in Syria has been heavily influenced by international law, particularly the principle of non-intervention. This principle, as outlined in the United Nations Charter, prohibits states from intervening in the internal affairs of another state. However, there have been exceptions to this principle, such as in cases of humanitarian intervention or when a state poses a threat to international peace and security.

The intervention in Syria has also highlighted the role of great powers in shaping international norms and laws. The actions of great powers, such as the United States and Russia, have had a significant impact on the interpretation and application of international law. This has raised questions about the legitimacy and effectiveness of international law, particularly in cases where great powers have conflicting interests.

Another important aspect of this case study is the role of public opinion in shaping great power intervention. The intervention in Syria has been heavily influenced by public opinion, both in the intervening states and in Syria itself. Public opinion has played a crucial role in determining the scope and duration of intervention, as well as the overall strategy and goals.

In conclusion, the intervention in Syria by great powers has been a complex and multifaceted issue. It has highlighted the importance of international law and norms, as well as the role of public opinion, in shaping great power intervention. The case of Syria serves as a valuable case study for understanding the dynamics of great power intervention and its impact on conflict situations.

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, conflicts and crises are becoming increasingly complex and interconnected. In such cases, great powers may be forced to intervene militarily in order to maintain stability and protect their interests. # Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

## Chapter 15: Case Study - Intervention in Yemen




### Introduction

The intervention in Afghanistan by great powers has been a topic of great interest and debate for many years. This chapter will delve into the complexities of this intervention, examining the various factors that influenced the decision to intervene, the methods used, and the outcomes of the intervention. 

The intervention in Afghanistan is a prime example of the use of military force by great powers to achieve their strategic objectives. It is a case study that provides valuable insights into the dynamics of international relations and the role of military intervention in shaping global politics. 

This chapter will not only explore the intervention itself but also the broader implications of this intervention for international law, security, and development. It will also examine the lessons learned from this intervention and their relevance for future interventions by great powers. 

The chapter will be structured in a comprehensive manner, providing a detailed analysis of the intervention in Afghanistan. It will begin with an overview of the intervention, including the reasons for intervention and the methods used. This will be followed by a detailed examination of the intervention itself, including the military operations, the role of international actors, and the impact of the intervention on the Afghan people and the country as a whole. 

The chapter will also discuss the outcomes of the intervention, including its impact on regional and global politics, and the lessons learned from this intervention. It will conclude with a critical analysis of the intervention and its implications for future interventions by great powers. 

This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive study of the intervention in Afghanistan, shedding light on the complexities of this intervention and its broader implications. It is hoped that this chapter will contribute to a deeper understanding of the role of great powers in international conflicts and the impact of their interventions on the affected countries and the global community.




### Subsection: 15.1a Historical Context

The intervention in Afghanistan by great powers is a complex and multifaceted issue that requires a deep understanding of the historical context. The country has been a site of conflict and conquest for centuries, with various empires and powers vying for control. This historical context has shaped the country's political landscape and its relationship with the international community.

#### Ancient and Medieval History

Afghanistan has been inhabited since ancient times, with evidence of human settlement dating back to the Stone Age. The country was part of the Persian Empire, the Macedonian Empire, and the Roman Empire. The rise of Islam in the 7th century led to the conversion of the majority of the population, and the country became a center of Islamic scholarship and culture.

#### Modern History

In the 19th and 20th centuries, Afghanistan was caught in the power struggle between the British and Russian empires. The British, who controlled India, saw Afghanistan as a buffer state to protect their interests in the region. The Russians, on the other hand, saw it as a potential ally in their expansionist plans. This led to a series of wars and interventions, with the British ultimately gaining control of the country.

#### Soviet Intervention

The Soviet Union, seeking to maintain its influence in the region, intervened in Afghanistan in 1979. The intervention was part of their larger strategy to contain the influence of the United States and its allies in the region. The Soviets supported the communist government in Kabul, which was facing insurgencies from Islamic fundamentalist groups. The intervention was met with strong resistance from the Afghan people, who saw it as a foreign invasion. The Soviets ultimately withdrew in 1989, leaving behind a devastated country and a power vacuum that led to further conflict and intervention.

#### U.S. Intervention

The United States, along with other Western powers, saw the Soviet intervention as an opportunity to weaken their Cold War rival. They provided support to the Mujahideen, the Islamic fundamentalist groups fighting the Soviets. This support included weapons, training, and funding, which ultimately led to the Soviet withdrawal. However, the U.S. intervention also had unintended consequences, as it helped to fuel the rise of extremist groups such as the Taliban.

#### Current Conflict

The intervention in Afghanistan by great powers has continued into the present day. The U.S. and its allies have been involved in the country since 2001, when they invaded in response to the 9/11 terrorist attacks. The intervention has been marked by a complex and often contentious relationship between the U.S. and the Afghan government, as well as ongoing conflict with the Taliban and other insurgent groups.

In conclusion, the intervention in Afghanistan by great powers is a complex issue with a long history. The country's historical context, including its ancient and medieval history, as well as its modern history of intervention by various empires and powers, has shaped the country's political landscape and its relationship with the international community. Understanding this historical context is crucial for understanding the current conflict and the ongoing intervention efforts.





### Subsection: 15.1b The Afghan Conflict

The Afghan conflict, also known as the War in Afghanistan, has been a major focus of international intervention since the 1970s. The conflict has been marked by various interventions by great powers, including the Soviet Union, the United States, and more recently, the United States and its NATO allies.

#### The Soviet-Afghan War

The Soviet-Afghan War, which lasted from 1979 to 1989, was a major intervention by the Soviet Union in Afghanistan. The Soviets, seeking to maintain their influence in the region, intervened to support the communist government in Kabul, which was facing insurgencies from Islamic fundamentalist groups. The war was marked by a series of Soviet offensives and counter-offensives, with the Soviets ultimately withdrawing in 1989, leaving behind a devastated country and a power vacuum that led to further conflict and intervention.

#### The United States Intervention

The United States, along with other Western powers, saw the Soviet intervention as an opportunity to contain the influence of the Soviet Union in the region. The U.S. provided support to the Mujahideen, the Islamic fundamentalist groups fighting against the Soviets, in the form of weapons and training. This support was part of the U.S.'s larger strategy to contain the Soviet Union and its influence in the region. The U.S. intervention was marked by a series of covert operations, including the provision of weapons and training to the Mujahideen, as well as the use of air power to support the Mujahideen and disrupt Soviet operations.

#### The Post-Soviet Conflict

The withdrawal of the Soviet Union in 1989 left behind a power vacuum in Afghanistan, which led to further conflict and intervention. The Mujahideen, who had been fighting against the Soviets, turned on each other, leading to a series of civil wars. The Taliban, a fundamentalist Islamic group, rose to power in the 1990s, imposing a strict interpretation of Islamic law and gaining control of most of the country. The Taliban's rule was marked by human rights abuses and the suppression of women's rights.

#### The United States Intervention (2001-2021)

In response to the 9/11 terrorist attacks, the United States, along with its NATO allies, intervened in Afghanistan in 2001. The intervention was aimed at overthrowing the Taliban, who were believed to be harboring al-Qaeda, the terrorist group responsible for the 9/11 attacks. The intervention was marked by a series of military operations, including the invasion of Afghanistan, the overthrow of the Taliban, and the establishment of a new government.

The intervention has been marked by a long and complex conflict, with the Taliban regaining control of large parts of the country and the U.S. and its NATO allies facing challenges in establishing a stable and secure Afghanistan. The intervention has also been marked by controversies, including the use of drone strikes and the treatment of detainees at the Guantanamo Bay detention camp.

#### The Post-Intervention Conflict

The U.S. intervention in Afghanistan has been followed by a complex and ongoing conflict. The Taliban, despite being overthrown in 2001, have regained control of large parts of the country and have continued to carry out attacks against the U.S. and its NATO allies. The U.S. and its allies have faced challenges in establishing a stable and secure Afghanistan, with the conflict continuing to this day.

### Conclusion

The Afghan conflict has been a major focus of international intervention since the 1970s. The various interventions by great powers, including the Soviet Union, the United States, and more recently, the United States and its NATO allies, have had a profound impact on the country and its people. The conflict continues to this day, with the U.S. and its allies facing challenges in establishing a stable and secure Afghanistan.





### Subsection: 15.1c International Response

The intervention in Afghanistan has been a major focus of international intervention since the 1970s. The conflict has been marked by various interventions by great powers, including the Soviet Union, the United States, and more recently, the United States and its NATO allies.

#### The International Community's Response

The international community has been closely monitoring the situation in Afghanistan since the Soviet intervention. The United Nations, in particular, has been actively involved in the conflict, providing humanitarian aid and facilitating peace talks between the various factions involved in the conflict. The UN has also been instrumental in coordinating international aid and assistance to Afghanistan, particularly in the aftermath of the U.S. intervention.

#### The NATO Intervention

In the aftermath of the 9/11 terrorist attacks, the United States, with the support of its NATO allies, intervened in Afghanistan to overthrow the Taliban regime, which was harboring al-Qaeda, the terrorist group responsible for the attacks. The NATO intervention, known as Operation Enduring Freedom, was initially successful in overthrowing the Taliban regime, but the conflict has continued for over two decades, with the Taliban regaining control of large parts of the country in recent years.

#### The International Community's Role in the Post-Intervention Period

The international community has played a crucial role in the post-intervention period in Afghanistan. The U.S. and its NATO allies have provided significant financial and military assistance to the Afghan government, but the conflict has continued, with the Taliban regaining control of large parts of the country. The international community has also been involved in efforts to facilitate peace talks between the Afghan government and the Taliban, with the aim of ending the conflict and establishing a stable and secure Afghanistan.

#### The Role of International Organizations

International organizations, such as the United Nations, the World Health Organization, and the International Red Cross, have been actively involved in providing humanitarian aid and assistance to the Afghan people, particularly in the aftermath of the U.S. intervention. These organizations have also been instrumental in coordinating international aid and assistance to Afghanistan, working closely with the Afghan government and other international actors.

#### The Role of International Law

International law has played a crucial role in the intervention in Afghanistan. The U.S. intervention was justified under the principle of self-defense, as the U.S. argued that the Taliban regime was harboring al-Qaeda, which had carried out the 9/11 terrorist attacks. The intervention was also supported by the principle of humanitarian intervention, as the U.S. argued that the Taliban regime was committing human rights violations against the Afghan people. The intervention has raised important questions about the scope and limits of international law, particularly in the context of counterterrorism efforts.

#### The Role of International Communication and Coordination

The intervention in Afghanistan has highlighted the importance of international communication and coordination in responding to a complex conflict situation. The U.S. intervention, in particular, has been criticized for its lack of coordination with other international actors, leading to a prolonged and costly conflict. The Atlantic Storm exercise, conducted by the U.S. government in 2001, highlighted the need for better international communication and coordination in responding to a bioterrorist attack. These lessons are particularly relevant in the context of the intervention in Afghanistan, where better coordination between international actors could have led to a more effective and sustainable intervention.




### Subsection: 15.2a Actors and Interests

The intervention in Afghanistan has been a complex and multifaceted affair, involving a variety of actors with diverse interests. These actors have been instrumental in shaping the course of the conflict and have played a crucial role in determining the outcome of the intervention.

#### The United States

The United States has been a key actor in the intervention in Afghanistan. The U.S. intervened in Afghanistan in the aftermath of the 9/11 terrorist attacks, with the primary objective of overthrowing the Taliban regime, which was harboring al-Qaeda, the terrorist group responsible for the attacks. The U.S. has also been involved in efforts to stabilize the country and establish a democratic government. However, the U.S. intervention has been marked by significant challenges, including the ongoing conflict and the resurgence of the Taliban.

#### The Soviet Union

The Soviet Union was another major actor in the intervention in Afghanistan. The Soviet Union intervened in Afghanistan in the 1980s, with the aim of supporting the communist government in Kabul and suppressing the Mujahideen, a group of Islamic fundamentalists who were fighting against the Soviet-backed government. The Soviet intervention resulted in a decade-long conflict, which ultimately led to the Soviet withdrawal from Afghanistan in 1989.

#### The Taliban

The Taliban, a fundamentalist Islamic group, has been a key actor in the intervention in Afghanistan. The Taliban took control of Afghanistan in 1996, following the withdrawal of the Soviet forces. The Taliban regime was characterized by human rights abuses and the suppression of women's rights. The Taliban's rule ended with the U.S. intervention in 2001, but the group has continued to operate as an insurgent force, challenging the Afghan government and the international forces.

#### The Afghan Government

The Afghan government, led by President Ashraf Ghani, has been a key actor in the intervention in Afghanistan. The Afghan government has been instrumental in efforts to stabilize the country and establish a democratic government. However, the government has faced significant challenges, including the ongoing conflict and the resurgence of the Taliban.

#### The International Community

The international community, particularly the United Nations and NATO, has been a key actor in the intervention in Afghanistan. The international community has been involved in efforts to facilitate peace talks between the Afghan government and the Taliban, with the aim of ending the conflict and establishing a stable and secure Afghanistan.

### Subsection: 15.2b Strategies and Tactics

The intervention in Afghanistan has been marked by a variety of strategies and tactics employed by the different actors involved. These strategies and tactics have been instrumental in shaping the course of the conflict and have had a significant impact on the outcome of the intervention.

#### The United States: Military Strategies and Tactics

The United States has employed a variety of military strategies and tactics in its intervention in Afghanistan. These have included conventional military operations, such as the invasion of Afghanistan in 2001 and the subsequent efforts to overthrow the Taliban regime. The U.S. has also employed unconventional tactics, such as drone strikes and special operations, in its efforts to combat the Taliban and al-Qaeda. However, these strategies and tactics have been met with significant challenges, including the resurgence of the Taliban and the ongoing conflict.

#### The Soviet Union: Conventional Warfare

The Soviet Union employed conventional warfare in its intervention in Afghanistan. The Soviet forces engaged in a full-scale invasion of Afghanistan in 1979, with the aim of supporting the communist government in Kabul and suppressing the Mujahideen. The Soviet forces employed a variety of conventional tactics, including artillery and air strikes, in their efforts to combat the Mujahideen. However, the Soviet intervention resulted in a decade-long conflict, which ultimately led to the Soviet withdrawal from Afghanistan in 1989.

#### The Taliban: Guerrilla Warfare

The Taliban has employed guerrilla warfare in its intervention in Afghanistan. The Taliban's tactics have included hit-and-run attacks, ambushes, and the use of improvised explosive devices (IEDs). These tactics have been instrumental in the Taliban's ability to resist the U.S. and Afghan government forces, and have contributed to the ongoing conflict in Afghanistan.

#### The Afghan Government: Counterinsurgency

The Afghan government, led by President Ashraf Ghani, has employed counterinsurgency strategies and tactics in its efforts to stabilize the country and combat the Taliban. These have included efforts to build up the Afghan National Security Forces, as well as efforts to win the support of the Afghan population through development and governance initiatives. However, these strategies and tactics have faced significant challenges, including the ongoing conflict and the resurgence of the Taliban.

### Subsection: 15.2c Outcomes and Impacts

The intervention in Afghanistan has had significant outcomes and impacts, both for the country itself and for the international community. These outcomes and impacts have been shaped by the strategies and tactics employed by the different actors involved, as well as by the broader political and social context in which the intervention has taken place.

#### The United States: Political and Social Impacts

The United States' intervention in Afghanistan has had significant political and social impacts. The U.S. intervention has been instrumental in the overthrow of the Taliban regime, which had been harboring al-Qaeda, the terrorist group responsible for the 9/11 attacks. However, the ongoing conflict in Afghanistan has also resulted in significant political instability and social unrest in the country. The U.S. intervention has also had significant social impacts, particularly for the Afghan population, who have been caught in the midst of the conflict.

#### The Soviet Union: Political and Social Impacts

The Soviet Union's intervention in Afghanistan also had significant political and social impacts. The Soviet intervention resulted in a decade-long conflict, which ultimately led to the Soviet withdrawal from Afghanistan in 1989. The conflict also resulted in significant political instability and social unrest in Afghanistan, which has had lasting impacts on the country.

#### The Taliban: Political and Social Impacts

The Taliban's intervention in Afghanistan has also had significant political and social impacts. The Taliban's rule, which lasted from 1996 to 2001, was characterized by human rights abuses and the suppression of women's rights. The Taliban's return to power in parts of Afghanistan since the U.S. withdrawal in 2021 has also resulted in significant political instability and social unrest in the country.

#### The Afghan Government: Political and Social Impacts

The Afghan government, led by President Ashraf Ghani, has also faced significant political and social impacts as a result of the intervention in Afghanistan. The ongoing conflict and the resurgence of the Taliban have resulted in significant political instability and social unrest in the country. The government's efforts to stabilize the country and combat the Taliban have also faced significant challenges, including corruption and lack of support from the Afghan population.

### Conclusion

The intervention in Afghanistan has been a complex and multifaceted affair, with significant outcomes and impacts for the country and the international community. The strategies and tactics employed by the different actors involved have been instrumental in shaping the course of the conflict and the outcomes of the intervention. However, the ongoing conflict and political instability in Afghanistan highlight the challenges and limitations of intervention, and the need for a comprehensive and coordinated approach to addressing the root causes of conflict in the country.

#### Exercise 3

## Chapter: Chapter 16: Case Study - Intervention in Iraq

### Introduction

The intervention in Iraq, a country located in the Middle East, has been a topic of great interest and controversy in the international community. This chapter will delve into a comprehensive study of the intervention, providing a detailed analysis of the events leading up to the intervention, the reasons behind it, and the subsequent outcomes. 

The intervention in Iraq is a significant case study in the field of great power military intervention. It provides valuable insights into the complexities and challenges of intervention, and the potential consequences that can arise from such actions. The chapter will explore the various factors that influenced the decision for intervention, including political, economic, and humanitarian considerations. 

The chapter will also examine the military strategies and tactics employed during the intervention, as well as the role of international organizations and other countries in the intervention process. The chapter will further discuss the aftermath of the intervention, including the political and social changes that occurred in Iraq, and the impact of these changes on the region and the world.

This chapter aims to provide a balanced and objective analysis of the intervention in Iraq, presenting a comprehensive overview of the events and their implications. It is hoped that this study will contribute to a deeper understanding of the complexities of great power military intervention, and serve as a valuable resource for students, researchers, and policymakers interested in this important topic.




### Subsection: 15.2b Strategies and Tactics

The intervention in Afghanistan has been marked by a variety of strategies and tactics employed by the different actors involved. These strategies and tactics have been instrumental in shaping the course of the conflict and have had a significant impact on the outcome of the intervention.

#### The United States: Strategic Conquest

The United States has employed a strategy of strategic conquest in its intervention in Afghanistan. This strategy involves the use of military force to gain control of key areas and resources, with the ultimate goal of achieving strategic objectives. In the case of Afghanistan, the U.S. has used this strategy to overthrow the Taliban regime and establish a democratic government. However, the U.S. has faced significant challenges in implementing this strategy, including the ongoing conflict and the resurgence of the Taliban.

#### The Soviet Union: Strategic Defense

The Soviet Union employed a strategy of strategic defense in its intervention in Afghanistan. This strategy involves the use of military force to defend against external threats and protect key areas and resources. In the case of Afghanistan, the Soviet Union used this strategy to defend its interests in the region and support the communist government in Kabul. However, the Soviet Union ultimately failed to achieve its objectives due to the resilience of the Mujahideen and the support they received from the U.S. and other Western powers.

#### The Taliban: Guerrilla Warfare

The Taliban has employed a strategy of guerrilla warfare in its resistance to the U.S. intervention in Afghanistan. This strategy involves the use of small, mobile, and often hidden combatants to engage in hit-and-run tactics against a larger, more conventional enemy. The Taliban has used this strategy to great effect, managing to resist the U.S. and NATO forces for over a decade despite being significantly outnumbered and outgunned.

#### The Afghan Government: Stabilization and Reconstruction

The Afghan government, led by President Ashraf Ghani, has employed a strategy of stabilization and reconstruction in its efforts to rebuild the country after the intervention. This strategy involves the use of diplomatic, economic, and social measures to stabilize the country and rebuild its infrastructure. However, the Afghan government has faced significant challenges in implementing this strategy, including ongoing security concerns and corruption.

### Conclusion

The intervention in Afghanistan has been a complex and multifaceted affair, with different actors employing a variety of strategies and tactics. The U.S. has used a strategy of strategic conquest, the Soviet Union a strategy of strategic defense, the Taliban guerrilla warfare, and the Afghan government stabilization and reconstruction. Each of these strategies has had a significant impact on the course of the conflict and the outcome of the intervention.

### Subsection: 15.2c Outcomes and Impacts

The intervention in Afghanistan has had far-reaching outcomes and impacts, both for the country itself and for the international community. These outcomes and impacts have been shaped by the strategies and tactics employed by the different actors involved, as well as by the unique characteristics of the Afghan context.

#### The United States: Partial Success

The U.S. intervention in Afghanistan has been largely successful in achieving its strategic objectives. The U.S. has been able to overthrow the Taliban regime and establish a democratic government, albeit one that continues to face significant challenges. However, the U.S. has also faced significant setbacks, including the ongoing conflict and the resurgence of the Taliban. The U.S. intervention has also had significant humanitarian impacts, with thousands of civilian casualties and millions of displaced people.

#### The Soviet Union: Failure

The Soviet Union's intervention in Afghanistan was a resounding failure. Despite employing a strategy of strategic defense, the Soviet Union was unable to defend its interests in the region and support the communist government in Kabul. The Soviet Union ultimately withdrew from Afghanistan in 1989, having failed to achieve its objectives and having suffered significant military and economic losses.

#### The Taliban: Resurgence

The Taliban's strategy of guerrilla warfare has allowed it to resist the U.S. and NATO forces for over a decade. Despite being significantly outnumbered and outgunned, the Taliban has been able to maintain a presence in Afghanistan and has even regained control of certain areas. The Taliban's resurgence has had significant impacts on the country, including the ongoing conflict and the deterioration of human rights.

#### The Afghan Government: Challenges

The Afghan government, led by President Ashraf Ghani, has faced significant challenges in its efforts to stabilize the country and rebuild its infrastructure. Corruption, insecurity, and ongoing conflict have hindered the government's ability to implement its stabilization and reconstruction strategy. The Afghan government continues to face significant challenges, and the outcomes of its efforts remain uncertain.

In conclusion, the intervention in Afghanistan has had complex and multifaceted outcomes and impacts. The strategies and tactics employed by the different actors involved, as well as the unique characteristics of the Afghan context, have all played a role in shaping these outcomes and impacts.

### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have delved into the complex and multifaceted issue of intervention in Afghanistan by great powers. We have explored the historical context, the various actors involved, and the strategies and tactics employed. We have also examined the outcomes and impacts of these interventions, both positive and negative.

The case of Afghanistan serves as a microcosm of the broader issues surrounding great power intervention. It highlights the challenges and complexities of intervention, as well as the potential benefits and drawbacks. It also underscores the importance of careful planning, consideration of all available options, and a deep understanding of the local context.

As we have seen, intervention in Afghanistan has been a recurring theme throughout history, with different powers intervening for a variety of reasons. Each intervention has had its own unique characteristics and outcomes, but they all share a common thread: the need for careful consideration and planning.

In conclusion, the case of Afghanistan provides valuable insights into the dynamics of great power intervention. It serves as a cautionary tale, reminding us of the potential pitfalls and challenges of intervention, while also highlighting the potential benefits. It underscores the importance of a nuanced and context-specific approach to intervention, and the need for careful consideration of all available options.

## Chapter: Chapter 16: Case Study - Intervention in Iraq

### Introduction

The intervention in Iraq is a pivotal case study in the realm of great power military intervention. This chapter will delve into the intricate details of this intervention, providing a comprehensive analysis of the events leading up to it, the strategies employed, and the outcomes that ensued. 

The intervention in Iraq is a complex and multifaceted issue, with numerous actors and factors at play. It is a case that has been studied extensively, yet there are still many unanswered questions and debates surrounding it. This chapter aims to provide a thorough examination of the intervention, shedding light on the various aspects that contributed to its successes and failures.

We will explore the historical context that led to the intervention, including the political, economic, and social factors that influenced the decision to intervene. We will also examine the strategies employed by the intervening powers, including the military tactics used and the diplomatic efforts made. 

Furthermore, we will analyze the outcomes of the intervention, both in the short and long term. This includes the impact on the region, the stability of the intervened country, and the implications for future interventions. 

This chapter will not only provide a detailed account of the intervention in Iraq, but also offer insights into the broader issues surrounding great power military intervention. It will serve as a valuable resource for those interested in understanding the complexities of intervention and its implications. 

Join us as we journey through this fascinating case study, exploring the nuances of great power military intervention in Iraq.




### Subsection: 15.2c Outcomes and Impacts

The intervention in Afghanistan has had significant outcomes and impacts on various stakeholders, including the Afghan people, the Taliban, and the international community.

#### The Afghan People

The intervention has had a profound impact on the Afghan people. The ongoing conflict has resulted in significant humanitarian crises, including food insecurity, displacement, and high mortality rates. The intervention has also led to the destruction of infrastructure and the disruption of economic activities, further exacerbating the humanitarian situation. Despite efforts by organizations like The Youth Cafe to provide aid and support, the overall impact on the Afghan people has been largely negative.

#### The Taliban

The intervention has also had significant impacts on the Taliban. The group has been able to resist the U.S. and NATO forces for over a decade, demonstrating its resilience and adaptability. The intervention has also led to the Taliban's expansion into neighboring countries, particularly Pakistan, where it has established safe havens and continued to carry out attacks in Afghanistan. The intervention has also resulted in the Taliban's evolution, with the group adopting more sophisticated tactics and strategies, including the use of improvised explosive devices (IEDs) and suicide bombings.

#### The International Community

The intervention has also had significant impacts on the international community. The U.S. and NATO forces have faced significant challenges in achieving their objectives, leading to questions about the effectiveness of military intervention as a strategy for achieving political goals. The intervention has also raised concerns about the use of drone strikes and the protection of civilian lives. The intervention has also led to increased tensions between the U.S. and Russia, with the latter accused of supporting the Taliban.

In conclusion, the intervention in Afghanistan has had significant outcomes and impacts on various stakeholders. While it has led to the overthrow of the Taliban regime and the establishment of a democratic government, it has also resulted in significant humanitarian crises and challenges for the international community.

### Conclusion

The intervention in Afghanistan has been a complex and multifaceted operation, with significant implications for both the region and the international community. The intervention has been marked by a series of strategic decisions, tactical maneuvers, and unintended consequences. It has also been characterized by a constant struggle to balance the interests of various stakeholders, including the Afghan government, the Taliban, and the international community.

The intervention has highlighted the importance of strategic planning and decision-making in military operations. It has also underscored the need for a comprehensive understanding of the local context, including the political, social, and cultural dynamics at play. Furthermore, the intervention has demonstrated the challenges of achieving long-term stability and security in a conflict-ridden region, even with the support of international forces.

In conclusion, the intervention in Afghanistan serves as a valuable case study for understanding the complexities and challenges of great power military intervention. It provides valuable insights into the strategies, tactics, and outcomes of such interventions, and offers important lessons for future interventions.
