# Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

## Chapter 16: Case Study - Intervention in Iraq




### Introduction

The intervention in Libya by great powers is a complex and multifaceted topic that requires a comprehensive study to fully understand its implications. This chapter will delve into the various aspects of this intervention, examining the motivations, strategies, and outcomes of the involved powers. 

The intervention in Libya is a recent event, occurring in the early 21st century. It was a significant event in the history of international relations, particularly in the Middle East and North Africa region. The intervention was led by a coalition of great powers, including the United States, France, and the United Kingdom, who intervened in Libya to protect civilians from the oppressive regime of Muammar Gaddafi.

This chapter will provide a detailed analysis of the intervention, starting with the historical context that led to the intervention. It will then delve into the motivations of the intervening powers, examining their political, economic, and humanitarian concerns. The chapter will also explore the strategies employed by the intervening powers, including military operations, diplomatic efforts, and humanitarian aid.

The chapter will also examine the outcomes of the intervention, both in the short and long term. It will assess the impact of the intervention on Libya, the intervening powers, and the international community. The chapter will also discuss the lessons learned from the intervention, and how they can inform future interventions by great powers.

In writing this chapter, we aim to provide a comprehensive and objective analysis of the intervention in Libya. We will draw on a wide range of sources, including primary documents, scholarly articles, and media reports, to provide a balanced and nuanced understanding of this complex event. We hope that this chapter will contribute to a deeper understanding of great power military intervention and its implications for international relations.




### Subsection: 16.1a Historical Context

The intervention in Libya by great powers is a complex and multifaceted topic that requires a comprehensive study to fully understand its implications. This chapter will delve into the various aspects of this intervention, examining the motivations, strategies, and outcomes of the involved powers. 

The intervention in Libya is a recent event, occurring in the early 21st century. It was a significant event in the history of international relations, particularly in the Middle East and North Africa region. The intervention was led by a coalition of great powers, including the United States, France, and the United Kingdom, who intervened in Libya to protect civilians from the oppressive regime of Muammar Gaddafi.

#### 16.1a Historical Context

The intervention in Libya was not an isolated event, but rather part of a larger historical context of great power intervention in the region. The region has been a site of intense competition and intervention by great powers for centuries. The Ottoman Empire, for instance, controlled much of the region until the early 20th century. The British and French empires also had significant influence in the region, particularly in Egypt and Algeria.

In the 20th century, the region became a site of intense Cold War competition between the United States and the Soviet Union. The US supported authoritarian regimes in the region, often at the expense of democracy and human rights. This support was often driven by strategic interests, such as access to oil and the containment of Soviet influence.

The intervention in Libya can be seen as a continuation of this historical pattern of great power intervention. The US, France, and the UK intervened in Libya not only to protect civilians, but also to protect their strategic interests in the region. These interests included access to Libya's oil reserves and the desire to prevent a humanitarian crisis that could lead to a refugee crisis and further instability in the region.

The intervention also occurred in the context of the Arab Spring, a series of pro-democracy protests and uprisings that swept across the Middle East and North Africa in 2011. The intervention in Libya was part of the international community's response to these protests, which aimed to protect civilians and support the transition to democracy.

In the following sections, we will delve deeper into the historical context of the intervention, examining the specific events and factors that led to the intervention. We will also examine the motivations and strategies of the intervening powers, as well as the outcomes of the intervention.




### Subsection: 16.1b The Libyan Conflict

The Libyan conflict, also known as the First Libyan Civil War, was a significant event that led to the intervention by great powers. The conflict began in February 2011, when protests against the regime of Muammar Gaddafi erupted across the country. These protests were part of the larger Arab Spring, a series of pro-democracy uprisings that swept across the Middle East and North Africa.

#### 16.1b The Libyan Conflict

The Libyan conflict was marked by a rapid escalation of violence. By the end of February, Gaddafi's government had lost control of a significant part of Libya, including the major cities of Misrata and Benghazi, and the important harbours at Ra's Lanuf and Brega. The government's forces, however, were able to push the rebels back and eventually reach Benghazi and Misrata. This led to an increase in the intensity of fighting and in the number of casualties, as warned by the president of the ICRC Jakob Kellenberger.

The conflict also saw the involvement of foreign military intervention. On 11 March, the Libyan Air Force was running out of quality jet fuel, and the government tried to bribe Maltese Air Force officials in order to buy fuel. This led to a multi-state coalition beginning a military intervention in Libya to implement United Nations Security Council Resolution 1973, which was taken in response to events then occurring during the conflict.

The intervention was initially largely led by the United States, with US forces and one British submarine firing cruise missiles. The Royal Canadian Air Force, French Air Force, United States Air Force, and British Royal Air Force undertaking sorties across Libya and a naval blockade by the Royal Navy. The effort was initially largely led by the United States. NATO took command of the intervention on 31 March, with the support of 17 states.

The intervention in Libya was a significant event in the history of international relations, particularly in the Middle East and North Africa region. It was a complex and multifaceted topic that required a comprehensive study to fully understand its implications. This chapter will delve into the various aspects of this intervention, examining the motivations, strategies, and outcomes of the involved powers.

### Conclusion

The intervention in Libya by great powers is a complex and multifaceted topic that requires a comprehensive study to fully understand its implications. This chapter has provided a detailed analysis of the intervention, examining the various factors that led to the intervention, the strategies employed, and the outcomes achieved. The intervention in Libya serves as a case study that highlights the complexities and challenges of great power military intervention.

The intervention in Libya was a significant event in the history of international relations. It was a response to the popular uprising against the regime of Muammar Gaddafi, which had been in power for over 40 years. The intervention was a joint effort by several great powers, including the United States, France, and the United Kingdom, who used military force to protect civilians and support the rebels.

The intervention in Libya was a success in terms of achieving its immediate objectives. The rebels were able to overthrow Gaddafi's regime, and the intervention prevented a humanitarian crisis. However, the intervention also had significant drawbacks. It was a costly operation, both in terms of human lives and financial resources. The intervention also led to a power vacuum in Libya, which has resulted in ongoing political instability and violence.

In conclusion, the intervention in Libya is a crucial case study for understanding great power military intervention. It highlights the complexities and challenges of such interventions, and the need for careful consideration of the potential outcomes and consequences.

## Chapter: Chapter 17: Case Study - Intervention in Syria

### Introduction

The intervention in Syria is a complex and multifaceted topic that has been a subject of intense debate and analysis in the international community. This chapter aims to provide a comprehensive study of the intervention, examining the various aspects of the conflict and the role of great powers in the region.

The intervention in Syria began in 2011 as part of the Arab Spring, a series of pro-democracy uprisings that swept across the Middle East. The conflict has since evolved into a complex civil war, involving multiple factions and external powers. The intervention by great powers, including the United States, Russia, and Turkey, has further complicated the situation, with each power pursuing their own interests and strategies.

This chapter will delve into the historical context of the conflict, examining the events that led to the intervention. It will also explore the various actors involved in the conflict, including the Syrian government, rebel groups, and external powers. The chapter will also examine the strategies and tactics employed by these actors, and the impact of their actions on the conflict.

Furthermore, this chapter will analyze the outcomes of the intervention, both in terms of the conflict itself and the broader implications for the region and the international community. It will also discuss the lessons learned from the intervention, and the implications for future interventions by great powers.

Through this comprehensive study, this chapter aims to provide a deeper understanding of the intervention in Syria, shedding light on the complex dynamics of the conflict and the role of great powers in the region. It is hoped that this analysis will contribute to a more informed and nuanced understanding of this important topic.




### Subsection: 16.1c International Response

The international response to the conflict in Libya was swift and multifaceted. The conflict, which began as a domestic issue, quickly escalated into a regional and then global concern. The international community, particularly the United Nations, played a crucial role in responding to the crisis.

#### 16.1c International Response

The United Nations Security Council, in response to the escalating violence and humanitarian crisis in Libya, passed Resolution 1973 on 17 March 2011. This resolution, sponsored by the United States, France, and the United Kingdom, called for an immediate ceasefire, the withdrawal of government forces from urban areas, and the establishment of a no-fly zone over Libya. The resolution also authorized the use of "all necessary means" to protect civilians and enforce the no-fly zone.

The international response was not limited to the United Nations. Several countries, including the United States, France, and the United Kingdom, began military operations in Libya. These operations were primarily aimed at enforcing the no-fly zone and protecting civilians. The United States, for instance, launched a series of airstrikes targeting Gaddafi's forces. France also conducted airstrikes and deployed ground troops to support the rebels.

The international response was not without controversy. Some critics argued that the intervention was a violation of Libya's sovereignty and that it was motivated by the desire to protect Western interests in the region. However, supporters of the intervention argued that it was necessary to prevent a humanitarian catastrophe and to uphold international humanitarian law.

The international response to the conflict in Libya highlights the complexities and challenges of international intervention. It underscores the importance of international cooperation and coordination in responding to crises. It also raises important questions about the role of international organizations, such as the United Nations, in these situations.




### Subsection: 16.2a Actors and Interests

The intervention in Libya was a complex affair involving a multitude of actors with diverse interests. These actors ranged from regional powers to international organizations and non-governmental organizations (NGOs). Each of these actors had their own reasons for intervening in the conflict, which often overlapped and sometimes conflicted with those of other actors.

#### 16.2a Actors and Interests

One of the primary actors in the intervention was the United States. The US had a vested interest in the region due to its significant oil reserves and its strategic location between Europe and Africa. The US also had a history of intervention in Libya, having supported the rebels during the Libyan Civil War in 2011. The US intervention was primarily motivated by its desire to protect its economic and strategic interests, as well as its commitment to promoting democracy and human rights.

Another key actor was France. France, like the US, had significant economic interests in Libya, particularly in the oil sector. However, France also had a historical connection to Libya, having been one of the colonial powers in the region. This historical connection, combined with its economic interests, motivated France to intervene in the conflict. France's intervention was also driven by its desire to protect its citizens, many of whom were expatriates living in Libya.

The United Kingdom was another major actor in the intervention. Like the US and France, the UK had significant economic interests in Libya, particularly in the oil sector. The UK also had a historical connection to Libya, having been one of the colonial powers in the region. However, the UK's intervention was also driven by its commitment to international law and its desire to uphold the principles of the United Nations.

In addition to these regional powers, international organizations and NGOs also played a significant role in the intervention. The United Nations, for instance, played a crucial role in coordinating the international response to the conflict. The UN Security Council's passage of Resolution 1973, which authorized the use of "all necessary means" to protect civilians and enforce a no-fly zone, was a key factor in the international intervention.

NGOs, such as the International Committee of the Red Cross (ICRC) and Médecins Sans Frontières (MSF), also played a crucial role in the intervention. These organizations provided humanitarian aid to the affected population and advocated for the protection of civilians. Their work was crucial in mitigating the humanitarian crisis caused by the conflict.

In conclusion, the intervention in Libya was a complex affair involving a multitude of actors with diverse interests. These actors, each with their own motivations and interests, worked together to address the crisis in Libya. Their collective efforts resulted in a complex and multifaceted intervention that had significant implications for the region and the international community.




### Subsection: 16.2b Strategies and Tactics

The intervention in Libya was a complex operation that required a multitude of strategies and tactics to achieve its objectives. These strategies and tactics were employed by the various actors involved in the intervention, each with their own unique approaches and goals.

#### 16.2b Strategies and Tactics

The United States, France, and the United Kingdom employed a combination of diplomatic, economic, and military strategies in their intervention in Libya. Diplomatically, they worked to garner international support for their intervention, particularly from the United Nations Security Council. Economically, they applied pressure on Libya through sanctions and the threat of further economic measures. Militarily, they conducted airstrikes and provided support to the rebels on the ground.

The US, in particular, employed a strategy of "leading from behind," where it provided support and guidance to the rebels, but did not commit significant ground forces. This strategy was driven by its desire to avoid a prolonged and costly intervention, as well as to minimize its own casualties.

France, on the other hand, employed a more direct approach, committing ground forces and conducting airstrikes. This was driven by its historical connection to Libya and its desire to protect its citizens and economic interests.

The United Kingdom also employed a combination of diplomatic, economic, and military strategies. Diplomatically, it worked to garner international support for the intervention. Economically, it applied pressure on Libya through sanctions and the threat of further economic measures. Militarily, it conducted airstrikes and provided support to the rebels on the ground.

In addition to these strategies, the intervention also involved a range of tactics, including the use of precision airstrikes, the provision of training and equipment to the rebels, and the implementation of a no-fly zone to protect civilians.

The intervention in Libya also involved a range of tactics, including the use of precision airstrikes, the provision of training and equipment to the rebels, and the implementation of a no-fly zone to protect civilians. These tactics were employed in conjunction with the overall strategies of the various actors involved, and were constantly adapted and adjusted as the situation on the ground evolved.

In conclusion, the intervention in Libya was a complex operation that required a multitude of strategies and tactics to achieve its objectives. The various actors involved employed a range of approaches, each with their own unique goals and motivations. The success of the intervention ultimately depended on the effectiveness of these strategies and tactics, as well as the cooperation and coordination between the various actors involved.

### Conclusion

The intervention in Libya serves as a case study that highlights the complexities and challenges of great power military intervention. The intervention, which was primarily led by the United States, France, and the United Kingdom, was aimed at protecting civilians and supporting rebel forces in their fight against the regime of Muammar Gaddafi. However, the intervention was not without its challenges, including the difficulty of achieving a clear and unified objective, the complexity of the local dynamics, and the potential for unintended consequences.

The intervention in Libya also underscores the importance of international cooperation and coordination in such interventions. The involvement of multiple great powers, each with their own interests and strategies, can complicate the intervention process. However, it can also bring a broader range of resources and perspectives to bear, potentially increasing the chances of success.

In conclusion, the intervention in Libya provides valuable insights into the dynamics and challenges of great power military intervention. It underscores the need for careful planning, clear objectives, and international cooperation in such interventions. It also highlights the potential for unintended consequences and the importance of adaptability in the face of changing circumstances.

### Subsection: 16.2c Outcomes and Impacts

The intervention in Libya has had significant outcomes and impacts, both in the short and long term. These outcomes and impacts have been shaped by the strategies and tactics employed by the various actors involved in the intervention, as well as the unique circumstances of the Libyan conflict.

#### 16.2c Outcomes and Impacts

The intervention has resulted in the overthrow of the Gaddafi regime, which had been in power for over 40 years. This has led to a power vacuum in Libya, with various factions vying for control. The country is currently facing significant challenges, including political instability, economic turmoil, and ongoing violence.

The intervention has also had a significant impact on the Libyan people. While it has led to the end of Gaddafi's regime, it has also resulted in a prolonged period of instability and violence. This has had a profound impact on the lives of ordinary Libyans, who have had to contend with the aftermath of the intervention.

The intervention has also had implications for the region and the world. The overthrow of Gaddafi has led to a shift in the balance of power in the region, with implications for neighboring countries and the global community. It has also raised questions about the role of international intervention in conflicts, particularly in the Middle East.

In terms of outcomes, the intervention has achieved its primary objective of protecting civilians and supporting the rebels. However, it has also resulted in unintended consequences, such as the ongoing instability and violence in Libya.

The intervention has also had significant impacts on the actors involved. The US, France, and the UK have all faced criticism for their involvement in the intervention, particularly in relation to the ongoing instability and violence in Libya. This has led to a reassessment of their intervention strategies and tactics, as well as a greater emphasis on diplomatic and economic approaches in future interventions.

In conclusion, the intervention in Libya has had significant outcomes and impacts, both for the country itself and for the international community. While it has achieved its primary objective, it has also resulted in a complex and ongoing situation in Libya, with implications for the region and the world. 


### Conclusion
In this chapter, we have examined the case of intervention in Libya by great powers. We have seen how the intervention was motivated by various factors, including humanitarian concerns, regional stability, and national interests. We have also discussed the different approaches taken by the intervening powers, with some focusing on diplomatic efforts and others opting for military intervention. The outcome of the intervention has been mixed, with some successes and failures.

The case of Libya highlights the complexities and challenges of great power intervention. It also underscores the importance of careful consideration and planning before engaging in such interventions. The lessons learned from this case can be applied to future interventions by great powers, helping to improve their effectiveness and outcomes.

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, the use of military force by great powers has become a common occurrence. Whether it is in the form of intervention in another country's affairs or in response to a threat to their own national security, the use of military force has become a powerful tool in the arsenal of great powers. However, the effectiveness of such interventions has been a subject of much debate and research. In this chapter, we will delve into a case study of intervention by great powers, specifically focusing on the intervention in Iraq. This case study will provide a comprehensive analysis of the various aspects of intervention, including the reasons for intervention, the methods used, and the outcomes and impacts of the intervention. By examining this case study, we hope to gain a deeper understanding of the complexities and challenges of great power intervention and its implications for the international community.

### Introduction

The intervention in Kosovo is a significant case study in the realm of great power military intervention. It serves as a prime example of the complexities and challenges faced by great powers when intervening in the affairs of another state. This chapter will delve into the various aspects of this intervention, providing a comprehensive analysis of the events leading up to it, the actions taken during the intervention, and the aftermath of the intervention.

The intervention in Kosovo was a multifaceted operation, involving not only military action but also diplomatic efforts, humanitarian aid, and peacekeeping operations. It was a pivotal moment in the history of international relations, testing the limits of international law and the effectiveness of international organizations. The intervention also raised important questions about the role of great powers in global conflicts and the ethical considerations of military intervention.

This chapter will explore these issues in depth, providing a detailed examination of the intervention in Kosovo. It will draw on a wide range of sources, including primary documents, scholarly articles, and firsthand accounts, to provide a balanced and nuanced understanding of this complex event. The aim is to provide a comprehensive study that will shed light on the dynamics of great power military intervention and its implications for global politics.




### Section: 17.1 Background:

The intervention in Kosovo was a significant event in the early 1990s, marking a turning point in the Balkans and the broader international community's approach to conflict resolution. This section will provide a historical context for the intervention, setting the stage for a more detailed analysis in the subsequent sections.

#### 17.1a Historical Context

The roots of the conflict in Kosovo can be traced back to the 14th century, when the region was part of the Byzantine Empire. However, the events leading up to the intervention in the 1990s were largely shaped by the aftermath of World War II and the subsequent breakup of Yugoslavia.

In the aftermath of World War II, the region was under communist rule, with Tito's Yugoslavia emerging as a socialist federation. However, upon Tito's death in 1980, the country began to unravel, with ethnic tensions and nationalist movements gaining momentum. The Albanian population in Kosovo, which had been suppressed under Tito's regime, began to demand greater autonomy and rights.

The situation deteriorated further in the 1980s, with the rise of Slobodan Milošević and his Serbian nationalist regime. Milošević's policies, which aimed to consolidate power and suppress ethnic Albanian separatism, led to increased tensions and violence in Kosovo. The Albanian population, which made up a majority in Kosovo, faced discrimination and violence at the hands of the Serbian-dominated security forces.

The situation in Kosovo came to a head in the early 1990s, with the Albanian population rising up against Serbian rule. The conflict quickly escalated, with both sides committing human rights violations and atrocities. The Serbian forces, under Milošević's command, carried out a campaign of ethnic cleansing against the Albanian population, resulting in the displacement of hundreds of thousands of people.

The international community, particularly the United States and NATO, became increasingly concerned about the situation in Kosovo. The conflict was seen as a threat to regional stability and a potential source of further instability and conflict. The United Nations Security Council passed Resolution 1199, calling for a ceasefire and negotiations between the Serbian government and the KLA. However, these efforts were largely unsuccessful, and the conflict continued to escalate.

The failure of diplomatic efforts led to the North Atlantic Treaty Organization (NATO) deciding to intervene militarily in Kosovo. This marked the first time in its history that NATO had launched an offensive without the approval of the United Nations Security Council. The intervention was aimed at protecting the Albanian population from further violence and pressuring the Serbian government to accept a negotiated settlement.

The intervention in Kosovo was a significant event in the history of international relations. It marked a shift in the international community's approach to conflict resolution, with the use of military force becoming a more prominent tool. The intervention also raised important questions about the role of international organizations, such as NATO and the United Nations, in conflict situations.

In the following sections, we will delve deeper into the events leading up to the intervention, the military operations, and the aftermath of the intervention. We will also examine the various factors that influenced the decision to intervene, including political, economic, and humanitarian considerations.

#### 17.1b International Response

The international response to the conflict in Kosovo was multifaceted and complex. It involved a range of actors, including the United Nations, NATO, and various European and non-European states. The response was shaped by a variety of factors, including the nature of the conflict, the perceived threat to regional stability, and the political and economic interests of the international community.

The United Nations, as the primary international organization responsible for maintaining international peace and security, played a crucial role in the response to the conflict in Kosovo. The UN Security Council passed several resolutions related to the conflict, including Resolution 1199, which called for a ceasefire and negotiations between the Serbian government and the KLA. However, these efforts were largely unsuccessful due to the intransigence of the Serbian government and the ongoing violence in Kosovo.

NATO, as the primary military alliance of the United States and its European allies, also played a significant role in the response to the conflict. In response to the failure of diplomatic efforts, NATO decided to intervene militarily in Kosovo. This marked the first time in its history that NATO had launched an offensive without the approval of the United Nations Security Council. The NATO intervention was aimed at protecting the Albanian population from further violence and pressuring the Serbian government to accept a negotiated settlement.

The NATO intervention was supported by various European and non-European states. The United States, as the dominant power in NATO, played a leading role in the intervention. Other key contributors included the United Kingdom, France, and Germany. The intervention was also supported by various non-NATO states, including Russia and China.

The international response to the conflict in Kosovo was not without controversy. Some critics argued that the intervention was a violation of international law, as it was launched without the approval of the United Nations Security Council. Others argued that the intervention was necessary to prevent further violence and protect the Albanian population.

Despite these controversies, the international response to the conflict in Kosovo set a precedent for future interventions. It demonstrated the growing role of international organizations, such as NATO, in conflict resolution and the increasing willingness of the international community to use military force to address security threats.

In the next section, we will examine the specific military operations carried out by NATO during the intervention in Kosovo.

#### 17.1c Lessons Learned

The intervention in Kosovo provides valuable lessons for future interventions by great powers. These lessons can be broadly categorized into three areas: strategic planning, international cooperation, and humanitarian considerations.

##### Strategic Planning

The intervention in Kosovo highlighted the importance of strategic planning in military interventions. The failure of diplomatic efforts to resolve the conflict underscored the need for a well-conceived and executed military strategy. The NATO intervention, while ultimately successful, was marked by initial setbacks and difficulties due to a lack of clear strategic objectives and planning. This experience underscores the importance of thorough strategic planning, including clear objectives, timelines, and contingency plans, in future interventions[^1^].

##### International Cooperation

The intervention in Kosovo also underscored the importance of international cooperation in military interventions. The involvement of various international actors, including the United Nations, NATO, and various European and non-European states, demonstrated the complexity of modern interventions. The intervention also highlighted the importance of coordination and cooperation among these actors to achieve common objectives. This experience underscores the need for effective communication, coordination, and cooperation among international actors in future interventions[^2^].

##### Humanitarian Considerations

Finally, the intervention in Kosovo highlighted the importance of humanitarian considerations in military interventions. The intervention was primarily aimed at protecting the Albanian population from further violence. This experience underscores the importance of humanitarian considerations in the planning and execution of interventions. It also highlights the need for effective humanitarian aid and support for affected populations during and after interventions[^3^].

In conclusion, the intervention in Kosovo provides valuable lessons for future interventions by great powers. These lessons underscore the importance of strategic planning, international cooperation, and humanitarian considerations in military interventions. They also highlight the need for effective communication, coordination, and cooperation among international actors, as well as the importance of humanitarian considerations in the planning and execution of interventions.

This section will provide a historical context for the intervention, setting the stage for a more detailed analysis in the subsequent sections.

#### 17.1a Historical Context

Milošević's policies, which aimed to consolidate power and suppress ethnic Albanian separatism, led to increased tensions and violence in Kosovo. This led to increased tensions and violence, as the Serbian-dominated security forces cracked down on Albanian separatism. The situation deteriorated further in the 1990s, with the rise of Slobodan Milošević and his Serbian nationalist regime. Milošević's policies aimed to consolidate power and suppress ethnic Albanian separatism, leading to increased violence and human rights violations against the Albanian population in Kosovo.

#### 17.1b The Kosovo Conflict

The Kosovo conflict, also known as the Kosovo War, began in 1998 and lasted until 1999. It was a result of the long-standing ethnic tensions and nationalist movements in the region. The conflict was primarily between the Albanian population, who made up a majority in Kosovo, and the Serbian-dominated security forces.

The conflict began when the Albanian population in Kosovo, who had been demanding greater autonomy and rights, rose up against Serbian rule. The Serbian security forces responded with violence and human rights violations, leading to a full-blown conflict. The conflict quickly escalated, with both sides committing human rights violations and atrocities. The Serbian forces, under Milošević's command, carried out a campaign of ethnic cleansing against the Albanian population, resulting in the displacement of hundreds of thousands of people.

The conflict also had international implications, as it was seen as a threat to regional stability and the potential for further escalation. The international community, particularly the United States and NATO, became increasingly concerned about the situation in Kosovo and the potential for further violence and instability in the region.

#### 17.1c International Response

The international response to the conflict in Kosovo was complex and multifaceted. The United States and NATO, in particular, played a significant role in the response. The US had a vested interest in the region, as it was seen as a potential source of instability and a threat to regional stability. NATO, as a security alliance, also had a responsibility to protect its member states and maintain regional stability.

The US and NATO initially attempted to resolve the conflict through diplomatic means, but these efforts were unsuccessful. As the conflict continued to escalate, the US and NATO began to consider military intervention as a last resort. This decision was made in part due to the failure of diplomatic efforts and the potential for further violence and instability in the region.

The US and NATO also faced pressure from the international community, particularly from European countries, to intervene in the conflict. The European Union, for example, passed a resolution calling for a ceasefire and negotiations between the Serbian government and the KLA. The US and NATO, however, were hesitant to intervene due to concerns about the potential for a prolonged and costly conflict.

In the end, the US and NATO decided to intervene in the conflict, with the goal of protecting the Albanian population and maintaining regional stability. This decision was made in part due to the failure of diplomatic efforts and the potential for further violence and instability in the region. The US and NATO also faced pressure from the international community, particularly from European countries, to intervene in the conflict.

The intervention in Kosovo was a significant event in the early 1990s, marking a turning point in the Balkans and the broader international community's approach to conflict resolution. It also set the stage for future interventions by great powers in conflicts around the world. 





#### 17.1c International Response

The intervention in Kosovo was a significant event in the early 1990s, marking a turning point in the Balkans and the broader international community's approach to conflict resolution. The international response to the crisis was shaped by a variety of factors, including the historical context of the region, the actions of key international actors, and the evolving nature of international law and norms.

##### United Nations Security Council Resolution 1170

The United Nations Security Council played a crucial role in the international response to the crisis in Kosovo. In 1998, the Security Council passed Resolution 1170, which welcomed the report of the Secretary-General on the situation in Africa and emphasized the need for a comprehensive response to the challenges facing the continent. The resolution also established a working group to review the recommendations in the report and consider ways of implementing them.

The resolution highlighted the responsibility of African leaders in regional conflicts and economic failures, and the dangers of foreign intervention. It also stressed the need for close cooperation between the Security Council and the Organization of African Unity (OAU) in conflict prevention. This resolution set the stage for the international community's response to the crisis in Kosovo, which was characterized by a focus on comprehensive solutions and close cooperation between international actors.

##### International Response to the Kosovo Crisis

The international response to the Kosovo crisis was shaped by a variety of factors, including the historical context of the region, the actions of key international actors, and the evolving nature of international law and norms. The intervention in Kosovo marked a significant shift in the international community's approach to conflict resolution, with a greater emphasis on humanitarian intervention and the protection of human rights.

The intervention was also shaped by the actions of key international actors, including the United States, NATO, and the European Union. The United States, under the leadership of President Bill Clinton, played a crucial role in advocating for intervention in Kosovo. NATO, under the leadership of Secretary General Javier Solana, also played a significant role in the intervention, providing military support and coordinating efforts with other international actors.

The intervention in Kosovo also marked a significant evolution in international law and norms. The intervention was justified under the principle of humanitarian intervention, which allows for intervention in a sovereign state to protect human rights and prevent humanitarian crises. This principle has been a subject of debate and evolution in international law, with the intervention in Kosovo serving as a key case study in its application.

In conclusion, the international response to the crisis in Kosovo was shaped by a variety of factors, including the historical context of the region, the actions of key international actors, and the evolving nature of international law and norms. The intervention in Kosovo marked a significant turning point in the Balkans and the broader international community's approach to conflict resolution, setting the stage for future interventions and shaping the evolution of international law and norms.




#### 17.2a Actors and Interests

The intervention in Kosovo was a complex affair, involving a multitude of actors with varying interests. These actors ranged from local ethnic groups to international organizations and states. Each of these actors had their own interests and motivations, which shaped their actions and responses to the crisis.

##### Ethnic Groups in Kosovo

The ethnic groups in Kosovo, particularly the Albanian and Serbian populations, played a significant role in the intervention. The Albanian population, which constitutes a majority in Kosovo, had been seeking greater autonomy and rights within Yugoslavia. The Serbian population, on the other hand, saw Kosovo as an integral part of Serbia and resisted any attempts at autonomy. The ethnic tensions between these two groups were a major factor in the outbreak of the Kosovo War.

##### International Organizations and States

International organizations and states also played a crucial role in the intervention. The United Nations, for instance, was instrumental in mediating the conflict and facilitating negotiations between the Serbian government and the KLA. The European Union, particularly Germany and France, also played a significant role in the intervention. Germany, for instance, was instrumental in providing logistical support and troops for the intervention, while France played a key role in negotiating the terms of the intervention.

##### NATO

NATO, as an international military alliance, was also a key actor in the intervention. The alliance was instrumental in providing air support for the KLA and in enforcing the no-fly zone over Kosovo. The intervention marked the first time in its history that NATO had launched an offensive without the approval of the United Nations Security Council.

##### The KLA

The KLA, or the Kosovo Liberation Army, was another key actor in the intervention. The KLA was formed in 1998 by Albanian nationalists seeking to establish an independent state of Kosovo. The KLA played a crucial role in the intervention by providing ground support and intelligence to the NATO forces.

##### The Serbian Government

The Serbian government, led by President Slobodan Milošević, was another key actor in the intervention. The government was responsible for the human rights abuses and ethnic cleansing that sparked the intervention. The government's actions were a direct response to the KLA's insurgency and its attempts to establish an independent state of Kosovo.

In conclusion, the intervention in Kosovo was a complex affair involving a multitude of actors with varying interests. Each of these actors played a crucial role in shaping the intervention and its outcome. Understanding the interests and motivations of these actors is crucial to understanding the dynamics of the intervention and its impact on the region.

#### 17.2b Strategies and Tactics

The intervention in Kosovo was a complex operation that required a multitude of strategies and tactics. These strategies and tactics were employed by both the international actors involved in the intervention and the local ethnic groups.

##### Strategies and Tactics of International Actors

The international actors involved in the intervention employed a variety of strategies and tactics. The United Nations, for instance, employed a strategy of mediation and negotiation in an attempt to resolve the conflict peacefully. This strategy involved facilitating talks between the Serbian government and the KLA, with the aim of reaching a mutually agreeable solution. The European Union, particularly Germany and France, also employed a strategy of mediation and negotiation, but with a focus on facilitating the terms of the intervention.

NATO, on the other hand, employed a strategy of air power and a no-fly zone. This strategy involved using air power to support the KLA and to enforce a no-fly zone over Kosovo. This was a significant departure from NATO's traditional role of defending its member states, and marked the first time in its history that the alliance had launched an offensive without the approval of the United Nations Security Council.

##### Strategies and Tactics of Local Ethnic Groups

The local ethnic groups in Kosovo also employed a variety of strategies and tactics. The Albanian population, for instance, employed a strategy of resistance and insurgency, with the KLA serving as their primary armed force. This strategy involved engaging in guerrilla warfare against the Serbian forces and seeking international support for their cause.

The Serbian population, on the other hand, employed a strategy of control and suppression. This strategy involved using military force to maintain control over Kosovo and to suppress the Albanian population. This strategy was largely successful until the intervention, when it was met with international opposition and military force.

##### Strategies and Tactics of the Intervention

The intervention itself employed a variety of strategies and tactics. The United Nations, NATO, and the European Union all played a role in the intervention, with each employing their own strategies and tactics. The intervention also involved a combination of diplomatic efforts, military operations, and humanitarian aid.

The diplomatic efforts involved mediation and negotiation, as well as efforts to gain international support for the intervention. The military operations involved air strikes and ground operations, with the aim of protecting the Albanian population and forcing the Serbian forces to withdraw. The humanitarian aid involved providing assistance to the displaced population and rebuilding efforts.

In conclusion, the intervention in Kosovo was a complex affair that required a multitude of strategies and tactics. These strategies and tactics were employed by both the international actors involved in the intervention and the local ethnic groups, and were crucial to the success of the intervention.

#### 17.2c Outcomes and Impacts

The intervention in Kosovo had significant outcomes and impacts, both in the short term and long term. These outcomes and impacts were largely a result of the strategies and tactics employed by the international actors involved in the intervention and the local ethnic groups.

##### Short-Term Outcomes

In the short term, the intervention resulted in a ceasefire and the withdrawal of Serbian forces from Kosovo. This was largely due to the strategy of air power and the no-fly zone employed by NATO. The air strikes and the threat of further military action forced the Serbian forces to withdraw, thereby ending the conflict.

The intervention also resulted in the establishment of a United Nations mission in Kosovo (UNMIK), which was tasked with overseeing the peace process and facilitating the return of displaced persons. This was a direct result of the United Nations' strategy of mediation and negotiation.

##### Long-Term Impacts

In the long term, the intervention had a profound impact on the political and social landscape of Kosovo. The intervention led to the establishment of an independent Kosovo, which had been a long-standing goal of the Albanian population. This was a direct result of the KLA's strategy of resistance and insurgency.

The intervention also led to a significant improvement in the human rights situation in Kosovo. The United Nations and other international organizations were able to monitor and report on human rights abuses, leading to increased accountability and improved conditions for the local population.

##### Impact on International Relations

The intervention in Kosovo also had a significant impact on international relations. The intervention marked the first time in its history that NATO had launched an offensive without the approval of the United Nations Security Council. This raised questions about the legitimacy of NATO's actions and the role of international organizations in conflict resolution.

The intervention also highlighted the importance of international cooperation in conflict resolution. The involvement of the United Nations, NATO, and the European Union demonstrated the need for a coordinated approach to addressing complex conflicts.

In conclusion, the intervention in Kosovo had significant outcomes and impacts, both in the short term and long term. These outcomes and impacts were largely a result of the strategies and tactics employed by the international actors involved in the intervention and the local ethnic groups.

### Conclusion

The intervention in Kosovo serves as a comprehensive case study of great power military intervention. It provides valuable insights into the complexities and challenges of such interventions, and offers lessons that can be applied to future interventions. The intervention in Kosovo was a multifaceted operation, involving not only military action, but also diplomatic efforts, humanitarian aid, and peacekeeping operations. It demonstrated the importance of international cooperation and coordination in such interventions, and highlighted the need for a comprehensive approach that addresses not only the immediate military situation, but also the underlying political, social, and economic issues.

The intervention in Kosovo also underscored the importance of understanding the local context and dynamics when planning and executing a military intervention. The intervention was successful in achieving its primary objective of protecting the ethnic Albanian population from violence and establishing a stable environment for the return of refugees. However, it also faced significant challenges, including resistance from local Serbian forces and the difficulty of operating in a complex and ethnically divided society.

In conclusion, the intervention in Kosovo provides a rich and complex case study of great power military intervention. It offers valuable lessons for future interventions, and underscores the need for a comprehensive and context-sensitive approach.

## Chapter: Chapter 18: Case Study - Intervention in Iraq

### Introduction

The intervention in Iraq, a pivotal event in the early 21st century, serves as a comprehensive case study for our exploration of great power military intervention. This chapter will delve into the intricacies of this intervention, providing a detailed analysis of the events leading up to it, the military strategies employed, and the aftermath of the intervention.

The intervention in Iraq was a complex and multifaceted operation, involving not only military action but also diplomatic efforts, economic sanctions, and humanitarian aid. It was a significant event in the history of international relations, with far-reaching implications for global politics and security. The intervention was a joint effort by a coalition of great powers, including the United States, the United Kingdom, and Australia, among others.

This chapter will explore the reasons behind the intervention, including the perceived threat posed by Iraq's weapons of mass destruction and its support for terrorism. It will also examine the military strategies employed during the intervention, including the use of air power, ground forces, and intelligence gathering. Furthermore, it will discuss the challenges faced during the intervention, such as the resistance of Iraqi forces and the difficulties of operating in a complex and hostile environment.

Finally, this chapter will analyze the aftermath of the intervention, including the establishment of a new government in Iraq, the ongoing security challenges in the country, and the broader implications of the intervention for international relations. It will also discuss the lessons learned from the intervention, and how these lessons can inform future interventions by great powers.

In presenting this case study, we aim to provide a comprehensive and objective analysis of the intervention in Iraq, shedding light on the complexities of great power military intervention and its implications for international relations. This chapter will serve as a valuable resource for students and scholars interested in international relations, military strategy, and conflict resolution.




#### 17.2b Strategies and Tactics

The intervention in Kosovo was a complex operation that required a multitude of strategies and tactics. These strategies and tactics were employed by both the intervention forces and the KLA, and they played a crucial role in the outcome of the conflict.

##### Strategies of the Intervention Forces

The intervention forces, primarily NATO and the United Nations, employed a combination of diplomatic, economic, and military strategies. Diplomatically, they sought to negotiate a peaceful resolution to the conflict, with the ultimate goal of establishing a stable and democratic Kosovo. Economically, they imposed sanctions on Yugoslavia, hoping to weaken the Serbian government and create conditions for a peaceful resolution. Militarily, they enforced a no-fly zone over Kosovo and provided air support for the KLA.

##### Tactics of the Intervention Forces

The intervention forces also employed a variety of tactics. Diplomatically, they engaged in shuttle diplomacy, with representatives of the United States, Russia, and NATO shuttling between Belgrade and Pristina to negotiate a settlement. Economically, they imposed a trade embargo on Yugoslavia, restricting its access to international markets. Militarily, they conducted a bombing campaign against Serbian forces in Kosovo, targeting their military and infrastructure.

##### Strategies of the KLA

The KLA, on the other hand, employed a combination of guerrilla warfare and diplomatic strategies. Guerrilla warfare was used to disrupt Serbian control of Kosovo and to create conditions for a negotiated settlement. Diplomatically, the KLA sought international recognition and support, particularly from the United States and NATO.

##### Tactics of the KLA

The KLA employed a variety of tactics. Guerrilla warfare involved hit-and-run attacks, ambushes, and sabotage. Diplomatically, the KLA sought to internationalize the conflict by appealing to international organizations and states for support. They also sought to portray themselves as the legitimate representatives of the Albanian population in Kosovo.

In conclusion, the intervention in Kosovo was a complex affair that required a multitude of strategies and tactics. The strategies and tactics employed by the intervention forces and the KLA played a crucial role in the outcome of the conflict.

#### 17.2c Outcomes and Impacts

The intervention in Kosovo had significant outcomes and impacts, both in the short term and long term. These outcomes and impacts were largely a result of the strategies and tactics employed by the intervention forces and the KLA.

##### Short-Term Outcomes

In the short term, the intervention resulted in a ceasefire and the withdrawal of Serbian forces from Kosovo. This was largely achieved through the diplomatic efforts of the intervention forces, particularly the United States and NATO. The no-fly zone enforced by NATO also played a crucial role in limiting Serbian military operations in Kosovo.

The intervention also led to the establishment of the United Nations Mission in Kosovo (UNMIK), which was responsible for administering Kosovo and overseeing its transition to democracy. The KLA, which had been fighting for independence, was integrated into the UNMIK as the Kosovo Protection Corps.

##### Long-Term Impacts

The long-term impacts of the intervention are more complex and multifaceted. On one hand, the intervention helped to establish a stable and democratic Kosovo. The KPC, for instance, played a crucial role in maintaining law and order in Kosovo during the transition period.

On the other hand, the intervention also led to a deepening of ethnic divisions in Kosovo. The KLA, which had been fighting for independence, was integrated into the UNMIK as the Kosovo Protection Corps. However, this integration was not without controversy, as many Serbs saw it as a betrayal of their interests.

##### International Impact

The intervention in Kosovo also had significant international impacts. It marked the first time that NATO had launched an offensive without the approval of the United Nations Security Council. This set a precedent for future interventions, particularly in the Middle East.

The intervention also led to a strengthening of the United States' position as a global superpower. The US played a crucial role in negotiating the settlement and in enforcing the no-fly zone. This was seen as a demonstration of US power and commitment to its allies.

In conclusion, the intervention in Kosovo had significant outcomes and impacts, both in the short term and long term. These outcomes and impacts were largely a result of the strategies and tactics employed by the intervention forces and the KLA.

### Conclusion

The intervention in Kosovo serves as a case study that highlights the complexities and challenges of great power military intervention. The intervention, which was primarily led by NATO, was aimed at protecting the ethnic Albanian population from violence and oppression by Serbian forces. However, the intervention was not without its challenges, including the difficulty of enforcing a no-fly zone, the need for a significant military presence, and the risk of escalation.

The intervention also underscores the importance of international cooperation and diplomacy in such interventions. The involvement of the United Nations and other international organizations was crucial in providing legitimacy to the intervention and in facilitating a peaceful resolution of the conflict.

In conclusion, the intervention in Kosovo provides valuable insights into the dynamics of great power military intervention. It underscores the need for careful planning, international cooperation, and a clear understanding of the local context. It also highlights the potential risks and challenges associated with such interventions, including the risk of escalation and the need for a significant military presence.

## Chapter: Chapter 18: Conclusion

### Introduction

We have examined a wide range of interventions, from the early days of colonialism to the more recent conflicts in the Middle East and Africa. 

In this final chapter, we will summarize the key findings of our study, highlighting the common themes and patterns that emerge from our analysis. We will also discuss the implications of these findings for future military interventions by major powers. 

While this book does not offer definitive answers to all the questions surrounding military intervention, it does provide a solid foundation for further exploration and discussion. It is our hope that this study will serve as a valuable resource for students, scholars, and policymakers alike, contributing to a deeper understanding of the role of military intervention in global affairs.

As we conclude this chapter, let us remember that the study of military intervention is not just an academic exercise. It has real-world implications that affect the lives of millions of people around the globe. By understanding the complexities of these interventions, we can better navigate the challenges they present and work towards more effective and ethical solutions.




### Subsection: 17.2c Outcomes and Impacts

The intervention in Kosovo had significant outcomes and impacts, both in the short term and long term. These outcomes and impacts were largely a result of the strategies and tactics employed by the intervention forces and the KLA.

#### Short-Term Outcomes

In the short term, the intervention resulted in a ceasefire and the withdrawal of Serbian forces from Kosovo. This was achieved through the diplomatic efforts of the intervention forces, particularly the United States and Russia, and the military pressure exerted by NATO. The intervention also led to the establishment of a UN peacekeeping mission in Kosovo, which helped to maintain stability and prevent further violence.

#### Long-Term Impacts

The long-term impacts of the intervention are more complex and multifaceted. On one hand, the intervention helped to establish Kosovo as an independent state, with its own government and constitution. This was a significant achievement, given the history of Serbian control over Kosovo. On the other hand, the intervention also led to a deepening of ethnic divisions in Kosovo, as the intervention forces were seen as favoring the Albanian majority over the Serbian minority. This has led to ongoing tensions and conflicts in Kosovo, particularly in the north of the country, where Serbian forces continue to maintain a presence.

#### Economic Impacts

The intervention also had significant economic impacts. The trade embargo imposed by the intervention forces led to a severe economic crisis in Yugoslavia, which contributed to the downfall of the Milosevic regime. However, the economic situation in Kosovo itself remains challenging, with high unemployment and poverty rates. The intervention also led to significant reconstruction efforts, which have helped to improve infrastructure and living conditions in Kosovo, but have also been criticized for being insufficient and inefficient.

#### Humanitarian Impacts

The intervention had a profound impact on the humanitarian situation in Kosovo. The bombing campaign conducted by NATO resulted in significant civilian casualties and damage to infrastructure. However, the intervention also led to the delivery of humanitarian aid to the population of Kosovo, which helped to alleviate the suffering caused by the conflict.

In conclusion, the intervention in Kosovo had significant outcomes and impacts, both in the short term and long term. While it helped to achieve a peaceful resolution to the conflict and establish Kosovo as an independent state, it also led to ongoing tensions and challenges. The lessons learned from this intervention are crucial for future interventions by great powers.

### Conclusion

The intervention in Kosovo serves as a case study that highlights the complexities and challenges of great power military intervention. The intervention, which was primarily led by NATO, was aimed at protecting the ethnic Albanian population from violence and discrimination by Serbian forces. However, the intervention was not without its challenges, including the difficulty of achieving a clear and unified strategy among the intervening powers, the need for a strong international legal framework to justify the intervention, and the potential for unintended consequences.

Despite these challenges, the intervention in Kosovo can be seen as a success in terms of its immediate objectives. The intervention helped to protect the ethnic Albanian population, led to the withdrawal of Serbian forces from Kosovo, and ultimately resulted in the establishment of an independent Kosovo. However, the long-term impacts of the intervention are more complex and include ongoing ethnic tensions and challenges to stability in the region.

The case of Kosovo underscores the importance of careful planning and consideration of potential consequences before engaging in great power military intervention. It also highlights the need for a strong international legal framework to justify such interventions and the importance of a unified strategy among intervening powers.

### Conclusion

The intervention in Kosovo by great powers serves as a case study that highlights the complexities and challenges of military intervention. The intervention, which lasted from 1999 to 2001, was a response to the ethnic conflict between the Albanian and Serbian populations in Kosovo. The intervention was led by the North Atlantic Treaty Organization (NATO) and involved airstrikes, ground operations, and peacekeeping missions.

The intervention in Kosovo raises important questions about the effectiveness and legitimacy of military intervention. The intervention was successful in achieving its primary objective of protecting the Albanian population from violence and establishing a stable environment for peacekeeping operations. The intervention was authorized by the United Nations Security Council, which provided a legal basis for the intervention. However, the intervention also faced criticism for its lack of a clear legal framework and the potential violation of international law.

In conclusion, the intervention in Kosovo serves as a valuable case study for understanding the complexities and challenges of military intervention. It highlights the need for careful consideration of the objectives, consequences, and legal framework of intervention, as well as the importance of international cooperation and diplomacy.

## Chapter: Great Power Military Intervention: A Comprehensive Study

### Introduction

In today's globalized world, conflicts and crises are becoming increasingly complex and interconnected. As a result, the use of military force has become a controversial and often debated topic among policymakers, scholars, and the general public. One of the most significant factors influencing the decision to intervene militarily is the involvement of great powers. These are countries with significant economic, political, and military influence on a global scale. Their actions can have far-reaching consequences and can shape the outcome of conflicts and crises.

In this chapter, we will delve into a case study of intervention by great powers, specifically focusing on the intervention in Iraq. This case study will provide a comprehensive analysis of the various factors that led to the intervention, the strategies and tactics used, and the outcomes and consequences of the intervention. By examining this case study, we hope to gain a better understanding of the complexities and challenges of great power intervention and its impact on global conflicts and crises.

Throughout this chapter, we will explore the historical context of the intervention, the motivations and objectives of the intervening powers, and the role of international law and organizations. We will also examine the effectiveness of the intervention and its impact on the region and the world. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a deeper understanding of the complexities and challenges of great power intervention and its role in shaping global conflicts and crises.

The intervention, which lasted from 1999 to 2001, was a response to the ethnic conflict between the Albanian and Serbian populations in Kosovo. The intervention was led by the North Atlantic Treaty Organization (NATO) and involved airstrikes, ground operations, and peacekeeping missions.

The intervention in Kosovo raises important questions about the effectiveness and legitimacy of military intervention. The intervention was successful in achieving its primary objective of protecting the Albanian population from violence and establishing a stable environment for peacekeeping operations. However, it also faced significant challenges, including the difficulty of achieving a clear and achievable objective, the lack of a clear exit strategy, and the unintended consequences of intervention.

The intervention in Kosovo also highlights the importance of international law and diplomacy in military intervention. The intervention was authorized by the United Nations Security Council, which provided a legal basis for the intervention. However, the intervention also faced criticism for its lack of a clear legal framework and the potential violation of international law.

In conclusion, the intervention in Kosovo serves as a valuable case study for understanding the complexities and challenges of military intervention. It highlights the need for careful consideration of the objectives, consequences, and legal framework of intervention, as well as the importance of international cooperation and diplomacy.

The intervention, which lasted from 1999 to 2001, was a response to the ethnic conflict between the Albanian and Serbian populations in Kosovo. The intervention was led by the North Atlantic Treaty Organization (NATO) and involved airstrikes, ground operations, and peacekeeping missions.

The intervention in Kosovo raises important questions about the effectiveness and legitimacy of military intervention. The intervention was successful in achieving its primary objective of protecting the Albanian population from violence and establishing a stable environment for peacekeeping operations. However, it also faced significant challenges, including the difficulty of achieving a clear and achievable objective, the lack of a clear exit strategy, and the unintended consequences of intervention.

The intervention in Kosovo also highlights the importance of international law and diplomacy in military intervention.
